# 1. THE 10X RULE -- Core Principles & B2B Application

## The Fundamental Law

The 10X Rule has two inseparable parts:
1. Set targets that are **10 times greater** than what you think you want
2. Take **10 times more action** than you believe is necessary to achieve those targets

## The Four Degrees of Action

Every person operates at one of four levels:

| Level | Description | Result |
|-------|-------------|--------|
| **1. No Action** | Do nothing. Wait. Hope. | Guaranteed failure |
| **2. Retreat** | Pull back from challenge. Reduce targets. | Slow death |
| **3. Normal Action** | Do what everyone else does. Average effort. | Average results (mediocrity) |
| **4. Massive Action** | 10X effort. Unreasonable activity. Obsessive execution. | Domination |

**The only acceptable level is Level 4: Massive Action.**

## Four Common Mistakes to Avoid

1. Setting sights too low
2. Underestimating required action
3. Competing instead of dominating the sector
4. Underestimating the adversity you will face

## Core 10X Principles

```
PRINCIPLE 1: Success is your DUTY, OBLIGATION, and RESPONSIBILITY.
             Not a choice. Not optional. It's what you OWE to yourself,
             your family, and your clients.

PRINCIPLE 2: There is NO shortage of success. One person's success
             does not reduce yours. Abundance mentality always.

PRINCIPLE 3: Never reduce a target. INCREASE ACTIONS instead.
             When results fall short, the answer is ALWAYS more action.

PRINCIPLE 4: The biggest business problem is OBSCURITY.
             Money and power follow ATTENTION.
             If nobody knows you exist, nothing else matters.

PRINCIPLE 5: Dominate, don't compete.
             Your goal is to SET the pace, not match it.
             Make competitors chase YOU.

PRINCIPLE 6: Obsession is a GIFT, not a disease.
             Society demonizes obsession. Cardone weaponizes it.

PRINCIPLE 7: Commit first. Figure out details later.
             Overthinking = death. Movement = life.
```

## B2B Application Framework

| Normal Approach | 10X Approach |
|-----------------|--------------|
| 10 prospect calls/day | 100 prospect calls/day |
| 1 market | 3+ markets simultaneously |
| 1 product line | Multiple complementary offerings |
| Hire conservative salespeople | Hire aggressive, high-volume sales talent |
| Follow up 1-2 times | Systematic follow-up: 12+ contacts |
| Compete on price | Compete on omnipresence and value |
| Wait for inbound leads | Create inbound + outbound + referral + social simultaneously |

### Key Quote
> "If people comment on your level of action, then you are doing something right."

---

# 2. SELL OR BE SOLD -- Key Frameworks

## The Core Philosophy

Everything in life is a sale. The primary reason businesses fail is an inability to sell enough. Your happiness and survival depend on your selling ability.

## The Three Levels of Salespeople

| Level | Characteristics |
|-------|----------------|
| **Amateur** | Uncommitted, lacks knowledge, reactive |
| **Professional** | Committed, knowledgeable, can predict outcomes |
| **Great** | Fanatic, masters prediction through obsessive observation |

**Formula:** Commitment + Knowledge = Prediction Ability

## Sell Yourself First (The #1 Rule)

```
"Only to the degree YOU are sold can you sell."

Before you can sell something to someone, you must first sell YOURSELF on it.
If you don't believe, buyers sense your lack of conviction.

Conviction = firmly held belief demonstrating COMPLETE AND UTTER CERTAINTY
that NO OTHER CHOICES appear available.

Be UNREASONABLE in your belief. Be FANATICAL.
Be willing to buy the product yourself at the price you're asking.
```

## The Agreement Principle (Most Important Rule in Selling)

```
"Always, ALWAYS, ALWAYS agree with the customer."

Process:
1. AGREE with the prospect
2. ACKNOWLEDGE their position
3. Make them RIGHT
4. THEN suggest alternatives suitable to you
5. Close the deal

"Like attracts like, and like is born out of agreement."
```

## The Perfect Sales Process (5-Step Framework)

```
Step 1: GREET the prospect
Step 2: DETERMINE wants and needs (LISTEN, don't sell)
Step 3: SELECT product and present/build value
Step 4: MAKE PROPOSAL (always, even tentatively -- absence of numbers prevents agreement)
Step 5: CLOSE transaction or prospect exits
```

## The Price Myth

```
Price is at the BOTTOM of reasons people don't buy.

Actual barriers:
- Unspoken objections (primary)
- Salesperson's own limiting beliefs
- Lack of confidence that the product solves their problem

"It's NEVER about price. It's about LOVE or CONFIDENCE
that the product will solve their problems."

"Your prospect, regardless of what he says, always wants MORE, not less."
```

## The People-First Business Model

```
"You are in the PEOPLE business first and the PRODUCT business second."

Selling is 80% people, 20% product.

Prospects care about:
1. Their time
2. Their money
3. What's best for THEM

YOU and your product rank far lower on their priority list.

"Be more interested in the customer than you are in yourself,
your sales process, your product, or your commission."
```

## Trust Through Documentation

```
"People believe what they SEE, not what they HEAR."

Rules:
- NEVER sell with words alone
- ALWAYS show documentation
- NEVER negotiate with words -- WRITE negotiations on paper
- Assume buyers NEVER believe your words initially
```

## The Giving Framework

```
"Selling is the act of GIVING, not getting; SERVING, not selling."

"Give, give, give is the assurance of sales, sales, sales."

Execution:
- Give ALL attention, energy, suggestions, information
- EXCEED expectations
- NEVER allow interruptions
- Show customers they are the MOST IMPORTANT person in your universe

"If you chase two rabbits at the same time, both will get away."
```

## The Hard Sell

```
"Most people will NOT buy without being asked."
"It has been said you have to ask someone FIVE TIMES before you get a yes."
"The moment you QUIT asking, the deal is DEAD."
```

## The Ten Commandments of Sales

1. Be proud and positive
2. Dress for sales success
3. See the sale (visualization)
4. Be sold on your offer
5. Know your value proposition
6. Always agree with your client
7. Super freak demonstration (enthusiastic product presentation)
8. Be time efficient
9. Assume the close
10. Always persist in the close

## Traits of Great Salespeople

- Willing to hear "no"
- Asks for the order regardless
- Listens selectively (to key information)
- Stays sold on their personal story
- Asks questions strategically
- Gets answers to their questions
- Knows price is not the issue
- Willing to pressure and persist
- Believes in selling as positive
- Trains and prepares constantly

---

# 3. THE CLOSER'S SURVIVAL GUIDE -- 120+ Closing Scripts

## The 20 Major Rules of Closing

Before the scripts, Cardone establishes that closing consumes only 10-20% of transaction time yet generates 100% of income. Pressure is necessary and vital to getting extra sales closed and removing time from the sales cycle.

## DELIVERY & LOGISTICAL CLOSES

```
DELIVERY CLOSE
"When would you like to take delivery of your new [product]?"
→ Assumes ownership. Offers options to say "yes."

IMMEDIATE DELIVERY CLOSE
"If there aren't any objections to moving forward with your new [product]
immediately, I will need your approval on the agreement."

TITLE AND REGISTRATION CLOSE
"Whose name would we be registering your new [product] in --
your name, your company's name, or both?"

PAPERWORK CLOSE
"Whose name will we be doing the paperwork in?"
→ Confirms decision-maker.
```

## AGREEMENT CLOSES

```
AGREEMENT CLOSE #1
"I agree it's [objection]. I need your okay here. Let's do this!"

AGREEMENT CLOSE #2
"I agree it's a lot of money, and I expect you knew it was a lot of money
before we set this meeting."

AGREEMENT CLOSE #3
"I agree, and everyone that has ever made this investment said the same thing."

WON'T BE THE LAST TIME CLOSE
"I agree, and this isn't the first time and won't be the last time
that you spend more money than you expected."
```

## FINANCIAL / MONEY CLOSES

```
CHECK CLOSE
"Would there be any other changes or additions you'd want me to make
on your [product] before we come to an agreement?"

SCALE OF 1-10 CLOSE
"On a scale of 1-10, how would you rate [product]? What would make it a 10?"
→ Identifies exact gap between where they are and closing.

PAYMENT CLOSE
"If the payments are not agreeable, we wouldn't expect you to buy."

BUDGET CLOSE #1
"Everyone who buys here is over budget. But we all still work it out.
We have a support group that meets here on Monday nights."
→ Uses humor to normalize being over budget.

BUDGET CLOSE #2
"You can probably say that about your credit cards, taxes, car payments,
insurance, house payments... but you still do them every month."

BUDGET CLOSE #3
"I understand, and expect that this decision will have plenty of company
at home and it won't be all by itself."

DOWN TO THE PENNY CLOSE
"We are within $XX.00 per month of you getting exactly what you want.
That's a minuscule amount. Let's do this!"

DELAY PAYMENT CLOSE
"[Name] will own now, assuming we handle X & Y and set it up so that
[Name] will not have any payments for the first 3 months."

NO EQUITY CLOSE
"Would you agree to owning your new [product], assuming we can arrange
financing with no money down?"
```

## SPOUSE / PARTNER STALL CLOSES

```
SPOUSE STALL CLOSE #1
"What if your spouse/partner says no?
A) Good, then I need your okay here.
B) Would your spouse say no to the product or the money?"

SPOUSE STALL CLOSE #2
"I agree, and you should talk to your spouse/partner. But if your spouse
is anything like mine, they would never tell me no when I love something."

SPOUSE STALL CLOSE #3
"I'm with you and I totally understand. But let me say this: it's better
to ask for forgiveness than it is to ask for permission."

SPOUSE STALL CLOSE #4
"Great, if you are anything like me, my spouse/CFO talk about everything!
Does your spouse/CFO already know you're here?"
```

## THIRD PARTY CLOSES

```
2ND PARTY ASSIST CLOSE
"[Look at 2nd party] At this figure, considering what you know about
this product, knowing what you know about [1st party], what advice
would you give them?"

UNAVAILABLE PARTY CLOSE #1
"The buyer agrees to ownership at figures and conditions spelled out.
Delivery is subject only to the unavailable party's approval. Is that fair?"

3RD PARTY CLOSE
"If I can get the seller to agree to what you are asking, would you agree
to close now? Sign here, here, and I'll see if the seller will agree."
```

## "THINK ABOUT IT" CLOSES (5 Variations)

```
THINK ABOUT IT CLOSE #1
"Thought is instantaneous. What you need to do now is make a decision.
It's not think time, it's yes-or-no time. It's do-or-don't-do time."

THINK ABOUT IT CLOSE #2
"I understand you need to think about it. However, your thinking won't
change the fact that this product saves you money and creates cashflow."

THINK ABOUT IT CLOSE #3
"Great, do you think 2-3 days is long enough, or would 2-3 weeks be better?
Let me ask you... May I share those with you?"

THINK ABOUT IT CLOSE #4
"Great, most people want to take time to think about their decisions.
Let me ask you, on a scale from 1-10, where would you be?"
→ Forces them to quantify their interest.

THINK ABOUT IT CLOSE #5
"I understand, and as a consumer myself, I have said the same thing...
There was a concern that still hadn't been addressed. Which one is it for you?"
→ Surfaces the REAL objection.
```

## EMOTIONAL / MOTIVATIONAL CLOSES

```
BE GRATEFUL CLOSE
"I agree with you. Now be grateful that you can invest this much money.
Not everyone can do that! I need your okay on the agreement."

CONGRATULATIONS CLOSE
"Yeah, I understand it's a big investment. And you should congratulate
yourself for being able to make an investment of this magnitude."

DO IT ANYWAY CLOSE
"I agree it's a lot of money. Do it anyway.
I understand this is over budget. Do it anyway."

DO IT FOR ME CLOSE
"Sir, if you can't do it for you, and can't do it for your wife, or your
company, then I'm going to ask you to do it for me."

TREAT YOURSELF CLOSE
"Of course it's a lot of money! And this isn't something you'd do every day.
Treat yourself!"

WORK HARD CLOSE
"I know it's a lot of money, I know it's more than you want to spend.
And this is why someone like you works so hard."

YOU DESERVE IT CLOSE
"I know you're over budget, and the fact is that you deserve it.
And if you don't deserve it, then I don't know anyone who does."

BETTER TO LIVE RICH CLOSE
"It's better to pay a little extra and get what you want than to pay
a little less and make a mistake. It's better to live rich."

CAN'T TAKE IT WITH YOU CLOSE
"I agree it's a lot of money. But let's face it -- you can't take it
with you. Let's do this!"

NO SHORTAGE OF MONEY CLOSE
"I agree it's a lot of money. But there is no shortage of money on
this planet. There IS a shortage of people that are happy."
```

## ASSUMPTIVE / COMMITMENT CLOSES

```
THREE YES'S CLOSE
"Did I answer all your questions? Were we easy to get to? Am I the type
of person you feel comfortable serving you? Good, then I need your okay."

HANDSHAKE CLOSE
"You know it serves your needs, you know you can afford it, it's only
a matter of time before you do it. Let's get this done.
[Reach out with open hand]"

MINOR POINT CLOSE
"Do you like the color? Do you like the size? Can you see yourself using
it daily/weekly? Let's get it wrapped up."
```

## DECISION-FORCING CLOSES

```
REASON TO BUY CLOSE
"May I ask -- are you looking for reasons to MAKE a decision today,
or are you looking for reasons to NOT make a decision?
What are the reasons to do this?"

IF I COULD, WOULD YOU CLOSE
"If I could handle every objection you had, if I could handle and get you
every request you've had, would you make a decision to invest?"

11TH INNING CLOSE
"What figures and terms would be necessary for you to say yes
to this investment?"

EVERYTHING THE SAME CLOSE
"If everything were the same, which product and who would you rather
buy from? Why else?"

MONEY EQUAL CLOSE
"If the money was the same, which product would you rather own,
or who would you rather buy from?"
```

## COMPETITOR / COMPARISON CLOSES

```
SAME PRODUCT CLOSE
[Customer: "I have a better price from your competitor"]
"Okay, which would you rather own if the money were the same?
Why is that? Why else?"

VALUE EXCEEDS PRICE CLOSE
[Customer: "Competitor is cheaper"]
"I understand, and I assure you that there is a great difference between
what I deliver and what my competitor delivers."

IMPORTANT PERSON CLOSE
"Due to your stature and influence in town/our industry, we are going
to do something special for you that we don't normally do."
```

## URGENCY / SCARCITY CLOSES

```
SCARCITY CLOSE
"As you are aware, there is limited availability. There is huge demand
for this product, and I want to ensure that you are able to get what you want."

TAKE AWAY CLOSE
"Let me suggest that you DON'T do this right now. If you come back tomorrow...
if somebody already steps up and it's spoken for, you would have to take
that as a sign."

FIRST OR LAST CLOSE
"The reality is you're either going to buy this now or later.
The question is: do you want to be the FIRST or the LAST?"

SOONER OR LATER CLOSE
"The reality is you're either going to buy this sooner or later,
and you know it. You need it, you like it, you can afford it. Let's do this sooner."

NOW OR NEVER CLOSE
"This is the offer I'm making you for right this moment in time,
and it is a now-or-never offer. This expires when you leave here."
```

## WAIT / DELAY CLOSES

```
WAIT CLOSE
"Certainly you can do that. Let me just share what happens when you wait:
you and your company still need [product]. The cost alone over 6 months
will cost you $XX,XXX."

NOW AND LATER CLOSE
"Excellent, I would consider waiting on a decision like this too.
Let me show you the cost of doing it NOW versus the cost of doing it LATER."

DONE AND OVER CLOSE
"Of course you could wait. You don't have to decide right now. But I want
to get it done and over so YOU can put your attention on things more important."

NEVER THE BEST CLOSE
"There is NEVER a best time to make this decision, as you will always
have things going on. Let's do this now."
```

## PERSISTENCE / WON'T QUIT CLOSES

```
APOLOGY CLOSE
"I really need to apologize to you for not being able to come to terms.
Can I ask -- was it something I did? I tried really hard. Was it something
I failed to do?"

REFUSE TO BELIEVE CLOSE
"I refuse to believe that you aren't going to do this. It's the right
product, the price is great, AND I know you want and need it. Let's do this!"

CAN'T QUIT CLOSE
"Sir, I'm not going to quit on you. You're either going to buy from me
now, OR I'm going to call you every day until you do this."
```

## CONFIDENCE-BUILDING CLOSES

```
WHO TAUGHT YOU THAT CLOSE
[Customer: "Can't afford it"]
"[Look shocked] Who taught you to think like that? You can do anything
you want to do. You can afford whatever you want to afford."

ABLE CLOSE
"Sir, forgive me, but when you say you can't do it today, I've got to
tell you -- you are shocking me! You are one of the most competent,
most able, most intelligent people..."

INTELLIGENCE CLOSE
[Customer: "Need to think about it"]
"Sir, you are one of the most intelligent people that has ever sat
across from me. THIS will be another intelligent decision."

WON'T ALLOW CLOSE
"I understand your position. However, I CANNOT ALLOW you NOT to own this
product. It is the right thing for you and your company."

OWNERSHIP CLOSE
"[Name], I'm putting your name on this. I will not let someone else
get this product, as I know it's the right thing for you."
```

## RISK MITIGATION / TRIAL CLOSES

```
PUPPY DOG CLOSE
"Let me suggest that you take delivery and try it out for a month.
At the end of the month, you decide whether it's right for you or not."

FEEL, FELT & FOUND CLOSE
"I appreciate the way you feel. I've felt EXACTLY the same way...
UNTIL I found out that [price isn't getting lower / no more inventory /
never a best time]."

LEAVE IT UP TO THE BANK CLOSE
"It's obvious you are concerned about the money. Let me suggest --
since money is the issue, we leave it up to the bank. If the lender
approves the deal, then we do the deal."
```

## REDUCE TO RIDICULOUS CLOSE

```
"$1000 a month? That's ONLY $30 a day. You're going to be using this
every week, every day. It's $30 a day for [massive value description]."
→ Break the price into the smallest possible unit.
```

## PRESSURE CLOSES

```
PRESSURE CLOSE #1
[Customer: "Are you pressuring me?"]
"Not yet, but trust me, I am WILLING to resort to pressure
to get this done tonight."

PRESSURE CLOSE #2
[Customer: "Are you pressuring me?"]
"Please don't confuse my ENTHUSIASM, my INSISTENCE, and my CONFIDENCE
in my proposal with pressure."

PRESSURE CLOSE #3
"Not yet, but don't think I won't resort to it. If you prove yourself
capable of not making a decision... don't think I won't use pressure."
```

## BEN FRANKLIN CLOSE

```
"I understand how hard it is to make a decision. It is said that
Ben Franklin, when faced with big decisions, would write out the
PROS and CONS so he could get an accurate evaluation."
→ Then list all PROS heavily outweighing the CONS.
```

## SUMMARY / REFERRAL CLOSES

```
SUMMARY CLOSE
"Let me remind you of what we are giving you here:
[summarize 1, 2, 3 points]. I need your approval here and here."

REFERRAL CLOSE
"Before we get involved with the figures -- WHO do you know that may
be in the market for [product] like this?"
→ Gets referrals BEFORE negotiation begins.
```

---

# 4. SALES OBJECTION HANDLING -- The Cardone Method

## The 14 Rules of Handling Objections

```
1.  NEVER give any one objection too much power
2.  NEVER talk while the buyer objects
3.  NEVER take an objection personally
4.  NEVER handle more than one objection at a time
5.  NEVER make verbal solutions or offers
6.  NEVER abandon negotiations because of an objection
7.  NEVER disagree with the buyer
8.  NEVER confuse the person with the objection
9.  NEVER believe the objection will keep the buyer from buying
10. NEVER let the buyer get into a no-win situation
11. NEVER let the objection get you down
12. NEVER ignore an objection
13. NEVER quit communicating no matter what
14. NEVER blame the customer or other conditions
```

## The Master Formula: ALWAYS AGREE

```
Step 1: LISTEN (don't interrupt the objection)
Step 2: ACKNOWLEDGE (validate their concern)
Step 3: AGREE ("I understand, and I agree with you...")
Step 4: ISOLATE ("Is that your only reservation?")
Step 5: VALIDATE ("That's a legitimate concern...")
Step 6: PROBE ("Help me understand -- what specifically concerns you?")
Step 7: TIE DOWN ("If we could solve that, would you move forward?")
Step 8: JUSTIFY (build value that exceeds the objection)
Step 9: CLOSE (ask for the order)
```

## Handling Specific Objections

### "I Need to Think About It"

```
RESPONSE 1: "Thought is instantaneous. What you need to do now is make
a decision. It's not think time. It's yes-or-no time."

RESPONSE 2: "I understand. There was a concern that still hasn't been
addressed. Which one is it for you?"
→ Surfaces the REAL objection hiding behind the stall.

RESPONSE 3: "Great, most people want to take time. On a scale
from 1-10, where would you be?"
If they say 6-8: "What would make it a 10?"
If they say 9: "What's the one thing holding you back?"

RESPONSE 4 (Reason to Buy Close): "Are you looking for reasons to MAKE
a decision, or are you looking for reasons NOT to make one?"
```

### "It's Too Expensive" / "I Can't Afford It"

```
RESPONSE 1 (Agreement + Close):
"I understand, and I agree with you. I have felt the same way about
similar products that I purchased. Sign here and here."
→ If they protest further, THEN it may be a real objection.

RESPONSE 2 (Who Taught You That):
"[Look shocked] Who taught you to think like that? You can do ANYTHING
you want to do. You can afford whatever you want to afford."

RESPONSE 3 (Reduce to Ridiculous):
"That's only $XX per day. Less than your coffee. For something that will
[massive value description]."

RESPONSE 4 (Gratitude):
"Be GRATEFUL that you and your company are in a position to even
CONSIDER this investment. Not everyone can."

RESPONSE 5 (Do It Anyway):
"I agree it's a lot of money. Do it anyway."
```

### "I Need to Talk to My Partner/Spouse/Business Partner"

```
RESPONSE 1: "I agree, and you should talk to your partner. But if your
partner is anything like mine, they would never tell me no when I love
something this much."

RESPONSE 2: "Great. Does your partner already know you're here today?
[If yes] Then they already support this process. Let's get the details
sorted so you can present them with a clear plan."

RESPONSE 3: "I'm with you. Let's do this -- you sign the agreement now,
subject only to your partner's approval. That way you lock in today's
pricing and terms. Is that fair?"

RESPONSE 4: "Would your partner say no to the PRODUCT, or to the MONEY?
[If money] Then let's figure out terms that work for both of you."
```

### "Send Me Information" / "Send Me a Proposal"

```
RESPONSE 1: "I'd love to! What specifically would you need to see in that
information to make a decision? [...] Great, I have all that right here.
Let me show you now."

RESPONSE 2: "Absolutely. The best information I can send you is ME.
When can we sit down for 15 minutes?"

RESPONSE 3: "I will definitely do that. But I find that the best
information transfer happens in conversation. What are the 2-3 things
you most need answered before moving forward?"
```

### "I'm Not Interested"

```
RESPONSE 1: "I appreciate that, and most of my best clients said the
exact same thing the first time we spoke. The reason is they didn't
yet know [key value proposition]. Give me 30 seconds."

RESPONSE 2: "I understand. You're not interested YET because I haven't
shown you anything to BE interested in. Give me 2 minutes."

RESPONSE 3 (Agreement): "I hear you, and I completely understand.
The question is -- are you not interested in [product], or not interested
in having this conversation right now?"
```

### "We Already Have a Vendor/Provider"

```
RESPONSE 1: "Great, who are you using? [...] They're good. I'm not asking
you to replace them -- I'm asking you to COMPARE. If the money were the same,
which would you rather have?"

RESPONSE 2: "Perfect. That tells me you already understand the value of
[category]. The question is: are you getting EVERYTHING you need, or are
there gaps? What would you improve if you could?"
```

---

# 5. PHONE / VIDEO CALL SCRIPTS

## The Outbound Cold Call Script (Complete Structure)

### Phase 1: Greeting

```
"Hey [Prospect Name], this is [YOUR FIRST NAME] with [Company Name].
Thanks for taking my call. Do you have thirty seconds?"
```

**Rules:**
- Use FIRST NAME only (unless your company is famous)
- Thank them for taking the call
- Ask for a small commitment of time (30 seconds, not 5 minutes)
- Do NOT ask "How are you doing?" or make small talk

### Phase 2: Reason for the Call (The Hook)

```
"The reason for my call is to see when you could give me just a couple
minutes of your time so I could show you how [COMPANY] can help you
[BIG CLAIM / VALUE PROPOSITION]."
```

**The Big Claim must address their pain:**
- "...add an extra $XX,XXX in revenue this quarter"
- "...solve your biggest prospecting problem"
- "...reduce your [cost/time/waste] by [specific amount]"
- "...get [specific result] without [specific pain]"

**Rules:**
- Be clear on WHY you are calling
- Make your BIG CLAIM immediately
- Get it all out FIRST THING
- If you cannot sell your offer in 20 seconds, you don't know your pitch

### Phase 3: Qualification

```
"What are the two biggest recurring problems you've experienced
with [category relevant to your product]?"

"If you believed in magic and I could snap my fingers and solve ONE
problem for you, what would it be?"

"Why would you guys spend money on this?"
```

**Questions to AVOID:**
- "Can I help you?" (Answer: "No")
- "What is your budget?" (They don't know; start with past purchases instead)
- "Are you the final decision-maker?" (Causes them to lie or disengage)

**Better alternatives:**
- "What brings you in today?" (instead of "Can I help you?")
- "What did you pay for [similar product] in the past?" (instead of budget)
- "Who else besides yourself would be involved in this decision?" (instead of decision-maker)

### Phase 4: Set the Appointment

```
"Would you make time to meet me [today/this week] for [X] minutes?
I'd love to show you exactly how we can [solve their stated problem]."

[If they hesitate:]
"How about today at [time]? Or would [tomorrow at time] work better?"
```

**Rules:**
- ALWAYS offer TODAY as the first option (creates urgency)
- Once you get a day, offer ALTERNATIVE TIMES
- Let the PROSPECT pick the time
- Be specific: "15 minutes" not "a bit of your time"

### Phase 5: Lock the Commitment

```
"Great, [Day] at [Time]. Go ahead and write that down.
[YOUR NAME], [COMPANY], [DATE], [TIME].

Is there any reason you wouldn't be able to make it?"
```

**Why "Is there any reason you wouldn't be able to make it?"**
- Gets verbal commitment
- Surfaces potential cancellation reasons BEFORE they happen
- Creates psychological contract

## The Incoming Call Script

### When a Prospect Calls You

```
"Thanks for calling [Company], this is [Name].
What brings you to us today?"

[LISTEN to their response]

"Great, I'm glad you reached out. Let me make sure I get you exactly
what you need. A few quick questions..."

[Qualification questions]

"The only way we are going to earn your business is to give you exactly
what you want: the best price and the best service on the exact product
you want. When can you come in [or meet] so we can make that happen?"
```

## Video Call / Zoom Best Practices

```
RULES:
1. DRESS PROFESSIONALLY (no exceptions -- even from home)
2. Camera ON always -- yours AND theirs
3. Treat it like an in-person meeting
4. OVER-COMMUNICATE (body language is limited on video)
5. Share your screen to SHOW documentation (people believe what they see)
6. Send written proposal DURING the call, not after
7. Close ON the call -- do not let them "think about it" and call back
```

---

# 6. FOLLOW-UP PHILOSOPHY -- "Until They Buy or Die"

## The Core Philosophy

```
"Follow up until they BUY or DIE. No ghosting allowed."

Statistics:
- 48% of salespeople NEVER follow up with a prospect
- 80% of transactions happen on the 5th to 12th contact
- Average company takes 72 HOURS to follow up a lead
- Contacting within first 5-10 minutes increases close rate 900x
```

## The 7 Follow-Up Principles

### 1. TAKE ACTION
```
Stop planning. Start dialing. 48% of salespeople don't even make the call.
Simply picking up the phone puts you in the top half.
```

### 2. FREQUENCY LEADS TO GREATNESS
```
Most sales require 5-12 contacts. NOT one or two.
Each touchpoint builds familiarity and rapport.
Each contact refines your messaging to their specific needs.
```

### 3. GET REGULAR (Establish a Cadence)
```
Create a SYSTEMATIC follow-up schedule:
- Day 1: Call + Email (within 5 minutes if possible)
- Day 2: Follow-up call + Text message
- Day 4: Email with value content (article, case study)
- Day 7: Call + Personalized video message
- Day 14: Call + Email with new angle
- Day 21: Social media engagement + Call
- Day 30: "Checking in" call + Written note
- Day 45: Call with new offer/angle
- Day 60: Call + Email
- Day 90: Quarterly check-in
- Then monthly for 12 months
- Then quarterly indefinitely
```

### 4. DO NOT WAIT TOO LONG
```
Research shows 21x improvement in qualification rate when responding
within 5 minutes versus 30 minutes.
Speed capitalizes on existing momentum.
```

### 5. BE CREATIVE
```
Diversify beyond phone and email:
- Text messages
- Social media engagement (comment, DM, share their content)
- Personalized video messages
- Handwritten notes
- Event invitations
- Referral strategies
- Personal visits
- Short videos
- Mentions on social media
- Gift/book mailings
```

### 6. HAVE A PURPOSE
```
Each interaction must serve a GENUINE objective.
- New information to share
- Market update relevant to them
- Case study of a similar client
- New feature or offer
- Industry insight
- Personal congratulation (promotion, milestone)

NEVER call just to "check in" with nothing to offer.
```

### 7. LEAVE A MESSAGE
```
ALWAYS leave voicemails or send follow-up emails after attempts.
Busy decision-makers appreciate persistent visibility.
Messages serve as reminders about previously-discussed content.
```

## The Long Game

```
Grant Cardone has followed up with some clients for 10 YEARS
before they bought something.

His framework:
- 12+ contacts over 6 months for a single prospect
- Multi-channel approach (email + phone + text + social + in-person)
- NEVER remove a prospect from the pipeline unless they:
  a) Buy from you
  b) Die
  c) Explicitly and repeatedly ask to be removed

"Nobody is doing any real follow-up. That's your advantage."
```

---

# 7. PRICING & NEGOTIATION -- Never Lower Your Price

## The Core Principle

```
"NEVER lower your price. ADD VALUE."

Discounting does NOT add value. It reduces YOUR worth.
Before discounting, ALWAYS attempt to give something ELSE
as a way to add value to the offer.
```

## Why Price Is Never the Real Issue

```
"It's almost NEVER price. It's almost ALWAYS about:
- Your process
- Your ability to read people
- Your determination to close the deal"

"While a lower price is the POPULAR way to make a deal,
it is NEVER the reason someone buys anything."

"A purchase won't happen until your potential customer is SOLD ON THE VALUE
and, more importantly, CONVINCED your offer will solve their problems."
```

## The "One Thing" Negotiation Framework

```
Every deal comes down to FOUR things,
but only ONE THING matters.

Your job is to find THE ONE THING stopping them from signing.

WARNING: Clients won't give you "the one thing" the first time.
They'll throw RED HERRINGS:
- "It's the product" (when really it's the money)
- "It's the timing" (when really it's fear of commitment)
- "I need to think about it" (when really they have an unspoken objection)

Technique: Keep probing until you find the REAL reason.
"Is that the ONLY thing holding you back?"
"If we solved [that], would you move forward TODAY?"
```

## Negotiation Tactics

### The Value Stack
```
Instead of dropping price, ADD:
- Extended warranty
- Additional service
- Bonus training
- Priority support
- Extra units/features
- Extended payment terms
- Delayed first payment
- Personal attention guarantees

"Never lower your price. Add value."
```

### Double the Value Strategy
```
"If the product costs $20,000, make sure you DOUBLE that value
through your demonstration of the product.

No one spends $20,000 on something worth $20,000.
They only spend that much when they believe they're getting
something of value IN EXCESS of what they're spending."
```

### The Written Proposal Power
```
ALWAYS present proposals in writing.

"People believe what they SEE, not what they HEAR.
Your proposal is what finally makes the sale REAL to your prospect --
right there in black and white.

Simply having the terms laid out tends to push the customer
toward buying, even if they have objections."

Present a proposal to EVERY customer -- no matter what.
```

## Handling Price Objections (Scripts)

```
OBJECTION: "It's too expensive."

RESPONSE 1: "Compared to what? What are you currently spending on
[alternative/doing nothing]? Let me show you the cost of NOT doing this."

RESPONSE 2: "I agree it's a significant investment. That's exactly WHY
you should do it. Because you INVEST in things that matter."

RESPONSE 3: "Everyone who buys from us says the same thing initially.
Then they realize the RETURN makes it the best money they ever spent."

RESPONSE 4: "If the money was the same, which option would you rather have?"
→ This isolates whether it's TRULY about price or about something else.

RESPONSE 5: "I know it's more than you wanted to spend.
This is why someone like you works so hard."
```

---

# 8. MINDSET PRINCIPLES -- The Mental Game of Selling

## Success Is a Duty

```
"Success is your DUTY, OBLIGATION, and RESPONSIBILITY."

Not a choice. Not optional. Not something you "try."
It's what you OWE to yourself, your family, and your clients.

If you approach sales as optional, your results will be optional.
If you approach it as a DUTY, your results will be inevitable.
```

## The Obsession Principle

```
"Be OBSESSED or be AVERAGE."

Obsession is the single common factor that all hugely successful people share.

Society calls obsession unhealthy. Cardone calls it the ONLY path.

"If you've got the energy to continuously go relentlessly, then HARNESS it."
```

## Commitment Changes Results

```
"When your COMMITMENT LEVEL changes, so do your RESULTS."

Sales is not persuasion. It's SERVICE delivered through:
- Clarity
- Confidence
- Consistency
```

## The Fear Framework

```
"The great thing about fear is that it isn't real."

Fear is manufactured by your mind. It's not a physical barrier.

"The more you do that which you fear, the more COURAGEOUS you become."

ANTIDOTE: "Pure, massive action will drown fear in no time."

Courage is EXERCISED through action, not inherited as a trait.
```

## Environmental Control

```
"You are a product of ALL that you surround yourself with."
- TV, newspapers, friends, hobbies, family

"Thoughts come before actions, and your actions determine your life."

RULE: Protect yourself from negative information.
Be careful where you get advice when pursuing your dreams.
```

## Rejection Reframe

```
"You will only feel rejection as a negative sensation if you do NOT
take full responsibility for the situation."

Rejection is DATA, not failure.
Every "no" teaches you something.
Every "no" gets you closer to "yes."

Ask after rejection: "Why didn't you choose to move forward?"
→ The answer is a goldmine for improving your next pitch.
```

## Daily Preparation Protocol

```
1. DECIDE you are ultimately responsible for the sale
2. Make it your DUTY, OBLIGATION, and RESPONSIBILITY
3. Take MASSIVE ACTION followed by MORE ACTION until the sale closes
4. Accept NO EXCUSES, reasons, or logic for failure
5. Prepare DAILY to handle all obstacles, stalls, and barriers
6. Begin each day with AFFIRMATIONS reinforcing your sales capability
7. Record and review your calls -- identify improvement areas
8. Role-play objections for 30 minutes BEFORE greeting your first prospect
```

## Key Mindset Quotes (Use as Daily Affirmations)

```
"Your greatness is limited only by the investments you make in yourself."

"Never take the position that things just happen to you; rather,
they happen because of something you did or did not do."

"A great attitude is worth more than a great product."

"People will pay MORE for an agreeable, positive, and enjoyable
experience than they will for a great product."

"A product can be shopped, but a great attitude CANNOT.
A price can be beat, but a great attitude is PRICELESS."

"Your attitude precedes everything that happens to you in life."

"People will ALWAYS act according to YOUR attitude."

"No one will pay you for what you KNOW. They'll pay you for what you DO."

"Winning begets winning."

"Problems = Opportunities for Future Sales."
```

---

# 9. SOCIAL SELLING -- The Omnipresence Strategy

## The Omnipresence Doctrine

```
Your #1 problem is OBSCURITY. Not price. Not competition. OBSCURITY.

"If nobody knows you exist, nothing else matters."

The hierarchy:
1. Be KNOWN
2. Be THOUGHT ABOUT
3. Be CONSIDERED
4. Be the FIRST and DOMINATING choice

You must become OMNIPRESENT in your market.
```

## Content Volume Strategy

```
Cardone's daily content output (as reference):
- 50-75 tweets
- New video content on YouTube and Facebook
- Articles on Medium, LinkedIn, Entrepreneur Magazine
- Instagram posts and stories
- Podcast episodes

Result from a SINGLE DAY of massive content:
- 22,000+ new Instagram followers
- 800+ new YouTube subscribers
- 1,200+ new Facebook fans

"Tweeting twice a day isn't sufficient."
```

## Platform Strategy

```
Use ALL platforms, ALL the time.

Instagram: Creativity + engagement + contests + cross-platform promotion
YouTube: Position yourself as expert. Post videos of products/services.
LinkedIn: Publish articles, engage with decision-makers.
Twitter/X: High-frequency posting. Share insights constantly.
Facebook: Community building + video content.
TikTok: Short-form content demonstrating expertise.
Podcasts: Long-form thought leadership.

"I use ALL of them ALL the time until they no longer get me where I'm going."
```

## Instagram Sales Strategy

```
1. POST CONSTANTLY -- not 1x/day, but multiple times
2. Be CREATIVE -- don't post standard content
3. ENGAGE -- ask questions, run contests, prompt comments
4. CROSS-POLLINATE -- drive followers from one platform to another
5. Be PERSONAL -- show behind-the-scenes, daily life, personality
6. DOCUMENT, don't create -- share your actual work, meetings, results
7. DM actively -- don't wait for inbound messages
8. Story > Feed -- use Stories for immediacy and frequency
9. Video > Photo -- video gets more engagement and builds more trust
10. CTA in every post -- always direct people to take action
```

## Social Selling in B2B

```
The social selling funnel:
1. VISIBILITY: Post content that demonstrates expertise
2. ENGAGEMENT: Comment on prospects' posts, share their content
3. AUTHORITY: Publish case studies, results, testimonials
4. CONNECTION: Send personalized DMs referencing their content
5. CONVERSION: Move conversation to call/meeting

"Social media does not function as a direct sales engine.
It BUILDS strong brand awareness that CREATES sales opportunities."

"Most people aren't USING their social media channels.
They're being USED by them."
```

## The Content Creation Philosophy

```
"Your biggest problem is obscurity."

To overcome it:
- CREATE content every day
- PUBLISH on every platform
- ENGAGE with your audience
- RESPOND to every comment
- SHARE value before asking for anything
- Make it so that when people think [YOUR CATEGORY],
  they think YOUR NAME
```

---

# 10. PODCAST / YOUTUBE KEY TEACHINGS -- Extracted Insights

## The Cardone Zone -- Key Teachings

### On Selling
```
- "The phone does not work; it's the PERSON ON THE PHONE who's working."
- "If you can't close, you lose."
- Sales success comes from DAILY practice and discipline.
- Record yourself selling. Watch it. Cringe. Improve. Repeat.
```

### On Wealth Building
```
- "Feed the beast: when you value money and spend it on the right things,
  you get more of it."
- Invest revenue into assets that generate more revenue.
- Don't spend on liabilities (things that lose value).
- Business income funds investment income.
```

### On Competition
```
- "Don't compete. DOMINATE."
- Provide so much attention, follow-up, and service that competition
  becomes impossible.
- Create "only" practices -- things ONLY you do in your industry.
```

### On Taking Action
```
- "Show up and do something, even if you don't want to."
- Start to think BIG.
- Give back to someone you can help.
- The formula for success: appear + act + persist.
```

### On Problems and Economy
```
- "Problems are opportunities for future sales."
- "Your personal economy doesn't have to reflect the national economy."
- "Every resource goes to ADVANCE and CONQUER while others
  contract and retreat."
- Economic downturns are when the best businesses are built.
```

## The Power Base Teaching

```
Your POWER BASE = people who already know, like, and trust you:
- Family
- Friends
- Previous customers
- Service contacts

"The power base represents the EASIEST sales you're going to make
because you have a relationship with them."

Strategy:
1. Make a list of EVERY person you know
2. Ensure they know what products/services you offer
3. Contact them REGULARLY -- not just when you need something
4. Past customers with complaints = OPPORTUNITIES for another sale
5. Keep as much attention on people you just sold as those you want to sell
```

## Seven Rules of Selling (YouTube/Podcast Series)

```
RULE 1: Always Agree With The Buyer
RULE 2: Treat Everyone Like A Millionaire
RULE 3: Write Up Every Buyer (always present a written proposal)
RULE 4: Never Quit On A Buyer
RULE 5: Follow Up Every Buyer
RULE 6: Be Willing to "Hard Sell"
RULE 7: Become a Closing Machine

EXERCISE: Rate yourself 1-10 on each rule.
Focus on your WEAKEST area this week.
Track measurable metrics.
Repeat with next weakest area.
```

## Key YouTube Teachings on Negotiation

```
"In life, you don't get what's FAIR. You get what you NEGOTIATE."

Every deal comes down to 4 things, but only ONE matters.

Top 7 tactics:
1. The One Thing -- find the REAL barrier
2. Selfish Child -- persist like a child who wants candy
3. White Flag -- temporary strategic retreat to re-engage
4. Never Split the Difference (price) -- add value instead
5. The Walk-Away -- be willing to leave (creates urgency)
6. The Anchor -- set high initial expectations
7. The Reframe -- change how they see the investment
```

---

# 11. APPLICATION NOTES FOR BRAZILIAN PORTUGUESE B2B CONTEXT

## Cultural Adaptation Principles

### What Translates Directly
```
- The Agreement Principle works PERFECTLY in Brazilian culture
  (Brazilians value harmony and "jeitinho")
- The People-First approach (80% people, 20% product) aligns with
  Brazilian relationship-based business culture
- Follow-up persistence is ESSENTIAL in Brazil where decisions
  take longer and involve more stakeholders
- The Power Base strategy is EXTREMELY effective in Brazilian business
  where "indicacao" (referral) is king
```

### What Needs Adaptation
```
- Tone: American directness ("Do it anyway") needs softening
  Brazilian version: "Olha, eu entendo perfeitamente. E justamente
  por isso que acho que voce deveria seguir em frente."

- Pressure closes: Brazilian prospects respond better to
  CONFIDENT SUGGESTION than AGGRESSIVE PRESSURE.
  Instead of "Sign here now" → "Vamos formalizar para voce
  ja comecar a ter resultados?"

- The Hard Sell: In Brazil, "hard sell" feels pushy.
  Reframe as "DEDICATED FOLLOW-THROUGH" or "COMPROMISSO COM O RESULTADO."

- Time: Brazilian business culture is more flexible with time.
  Build in buffer for delayed responses. Follow up MORE, not less.
```

## Key Phrases Adapted to Brazilian Portuguese B2B

### Opening (Cold Call / DM)

```
ENGLISH: "Hey [Name], this is [You] with [Company]. Thanks for
taking my call. Do you have thirty seconds?"

BRAZILIAN B2B: "Oi [Nome], aqui e o [Voce] da [Empresa]. Obrigado
por atender. Posso tomar 30 segundos do seu tempo?"
```

### The Big Claim

```
ENGLISH: "The reason for my call is to show you how you can add
$50K in revenue this quarter."

BRAZILIAN B2B: "O motivo do meu contato e mostrar como [EMPRESA]
pode te ajudar a [RESULTADO CONCRETO] nos proximos [PRAZO].
Ja fizemos isso com [REFERENCIA/CASE]."
```

### Agreement Formula

```
ENGLISH: "I agree it's a lot of money."
BRAZILIAN: "Concordo totalmente, e um investimento significativo."

ENGLISH: "Everyone who buys here is over budget."
BRAZILIAN: "Todo cliente nosso disse a mesma coisa no inicio.
E todos eles tiveram retorno."

ENGLISH: "I understand you need to think about it."
BRAZILIAN: "Entendo perfeitamente. Me diz uma coisa -- de 0 a 10,
onde voce esta em relacao a isso?"
```

### Closing Phrases

```
ENGLISH: "Let's do this!"
BRAZILIAN: "Vamos formalizar? / Bora comecar?"

ENGLISH: "I need your okay here."
BRAZILIAN: "Preciso so da sua confirmacao aqui."

ENGLISH: "When would you like to take delivery?"
BRAZILIAN: "Quando voce gostaria de comecar a implementacao?"

ENGLISH: "Who's name will we be doing the paperwork in?"
BRAZILIAN: "Em nome de quem fazemos o contrato? Pessoa fisica ou CNPJ?"
```

### Objection Handling

```
"PRECISO PENSAR" (Need to think):
"Entendo. Normalmente quando alguem me diz isso, existe uma duvida
que ainda nao foi respondida. Qual e a sua?"

"ESTA CARO" (Too expensive):
"Concordo que e um investimento. E justamente por isso que vou te
mostrar o retorno. Quanto voce esta PERDENDO hoje por nao ter isso?"

"PRECISO FALAR COM MEU SOCIO" (Need to talk to partner):
"Perfeito. Seu socio ja sabe que voce esta avaliando isso?
[Se sim] Otimo, entao ele ja apoia o processo. Vamos adiantar os
detalhes para voce apresentar algo concreto?"

"MANDA UMA PROPOSTA" (Send a proposal):
"Claro! Inclusive, a melhor proposta que posso mandar e eu mesmo
explicando pessoalmente. Quando podemos agendar 15 minutos?"

"JA TENHO FORNECEDOR" (Already have a vendor):
"Otimo, isso mostra que voce ja entende o valor disso. A pergunta e:
voce esta tendo TUDO que precisa? O que melhoraria se pudesse?"
```

### Follow-Up Sequence (Brazilian B2B)

```
DIA 1:  WhatsApp + Email (dentro de 5 minutos se possivel)
DIA 2:  Ligacao + Mensagem de acompanhamento
DIA 4:  WhatsApp com conteudo de valor (case, artigo, insight)
DIA 7:  Ligacao + Audio personalizado no WhatsApp
DIA 14: Email com novo angulo + Engajamento no Instagram
DIA 21: Ligacao + Mensagem com case similar
DIA 30: "Check-in" WhatsApp + Convite para evento/live
DIA 45: Ligacao com nova proposta ou condicao
DIA 60: Email + WhatsApp
DIA 90: Follow-up trimestral

NOTA: No Brasil, WhatsApp substitui email como canal principal.
Adapte TODO o framework de follow-up para WhatsApp como canal #1.
```

### Brazilian B2B Specifics

```
IMPORTANT DIFFERENCES:
1. WHATSAPP is the #1 business communication channel (not email)
2. RELATIONSHIP ("relacionamento") comes before the sale
3. REFERRAL ("indicacao") is the most powerful lead source
4. CNPJ/CPF determines contract structure (ask early)
5. PARCELAMENTO (installments) is expected -- always offer
6. NOTA FISCAL is part of the close process
7. REUNIAO PRESENCIAL still carries more weight than Zoom
8. GRUPO DE WHATSAPP for client communities is powerful
9. Brazilian prospects test commitment through DELAY -- persist
10. PERSONAL TOUCH (birthday messages, holiday greetings) matters MORE
```

---

# QUICK REFERENCE: THE GRANT CARDONE CHEAT SHEET

```
BEFORE EVERY CALL:
[ ] Am I sold on my product? (If not, re-sell yourself first)
[ ] Do I know my Big Claim in under 20 seconds?
[ ] Do I have 5 responses ready for top objections?
[ ] Do I have my written proposal ready to present?
[ ] Am I in a state of CERTAINTY and CONVICTION?

DURING EVERY CALL:
[ ] Greet → Reason → Qualify → Present → Close
[ ] ALWAYS AGREE first, then redirect
[ ] SHOW, don't just tell (documentation, screen share, proposals)
[ ] Ask for the sale AT LEAST 5 times
[ ] If they say "think about it" → surface the REAL objection
[ ] NEVER leave without a next step or signed agreement

AFTER EVERY CALL:
[ ] Log in CRM within 5 minutes
[ ] Schedule next follow-up touchpoint
[ ] Send written summary of what was discussed
[ ] Note objections heard (build your objection notebook)
[ ] Rate yourself 1-10 on performance -- what would make it a 10?

DAILY HABITS:
[ ] 30 minutes of roleplay/objection drilling BEFORE first call
[ ] 10X your target: if goal is 10 calls, make 100
[ ] Review yesterday's recordings -- identify 1 improvement
[ ] Post content on social media (minimum 3x per platform)
[ ] Contact your Power Base (past clients, referrals)
[ ] End day by preparing tomorrow's prospect list
```

---

# PART 2: JORDAN BELFORT -- Straight Line Selling System

# JORDAN BELFORT'S STRAIGHT LINE SELLING SYSTEM
## Complete Deep Research -- Actionable Playbook

---

## TABLE OF CONTENTS

1. The Straight Line System (Core Framework)
2. The Three Tens (Certainty Scale)
3. The First Four Seconds
4. The Four Buyer Archetypes
5. Ten Core Influencing Tonalities
6. Body Language Mastery
7. State Management and NLP Anchoring
8. Intelligence Gathering and Qualifying
9. The Ten Rules of Straight Line Prospecting
10. Script Architecture
11. The Looping Technique (Objection Handling)
12. Action Threshold and Pain Threshold
13. Ethical Persuasion Principles
14. Key Power Phrases
15. Podcast/YouTube Key Insights
16. Application Notes for Brazilian B2B Context
