## 1. FANATICAL PROSPECTING -- CORE FRAMEWORK

### The Universal Truth

The number one reason for failure in sales is an empty pipeline. And the number one reason for an empty pipeline is the failure to consistently prospect. Everything in Jeb Blount's system flows from this single premise.

### Seven Mindsets of Fanatical Prospectors

1. **Optimistic & Enthusiastic** -- Winning, positive energy attracts prospects
2. **Competitive** -- Fierce competitor mentality; treat prospecting like a sport
3. **Confident** -- Unshakeable belief in your approach and value
4. **Relentless** -- Never stop, never quit, one more call
5. **Thirsty for Knowledge** -- Continuous improvement, always learning
6. **Systematic & Efficient** -- Organized, process-driven, metrics-obsessed
7. **Adaptive & Flexible** -- Adjust to context while maintaining discipline

### The Three Universal Laws of Sales

**Law of Need** -- The more desperate you are, the less likely you are to close. Desperation repels prospects. Detachment improves outcomes. Keep the pipeline full so you never negotiate from a position of need.

**Law of Replacement** -- Continuously inject new opportunities into the pipeline at rates that match or exceed your closing ratios. Every deal that closes or falls out must be replaced immediately.

**Law of Familiarity** -- Persistent, consistent contact builds relationships. It takes 20-50 touches to engage a cold prospect who has never heard of you. Familiarity breeds trust, not contempt.

### The Four Objectives of Prospecting

Every prospecting activity should accomplish one of these:

1. **Set an appointment** with a decision maker
2. **Gather information** and qualify the prospect
3. **Close a sale** (for transactional/lower-price offerings)
4. **Build familiarity** through repeated touchpoints

### The Prospecting Pyramid (Qualification Tiers)

```
         /\
        /  \     PEAK: Hot leads, referrals -- ready to buy
       /    \    PRIORITIZE: Immediate pipeline advancement
      /------\
     /        \   TIER 3: Warm prospects -- nurture relationships
    /          \  Monitor purchase-readiness signals
   /------------\
  /              \  TIER 2: Known decision makers, budget identified
 /                \ Ask qualifying questions, prepare for advancement
/------------------\
 TIER 1 (BASE):      Prospects you barely know
 Gather info, qualify, build familiarity
```

**Strategy:** Focus 10-20% of effort on top tier for highest conversion return. Work top-down with organized lists. Never waste time on unqualified prospects when qualified ones are available.

### The Three Enemies of Prospecting (The 3 P's)

1. **Procrastination** -- "I'll do it later." Break work into small bites; prospect daily.
2. **Perfectionism** -- "I need to prepare more." Activity beats perfection. Sandra made 53 conversations in 1 hour, engaged 14 decision makers, booked 2 appointments. Jeremy spent 3 hours reviewing notes, made 7 calls, booked zero.
3. **Paralysis by Analysis** -- "What if they say no?" Focus on one call at a time. Avoid "what if" scenarios.

### Time Management: Golden Hours and Platinum Hours

**Golden Hours** = Revenue-Generating Activities (RGA)
- Protected time blocks dedicated EXCLUSIVELY to prospecting and customer engagement
- No admin, no email, no internal meetings
- Typically: 8:00-10:00 AM and 4:00-6:00 PM (when prospects are accessible)
- This is NON-NEGOTIABLE time

**Platinum Hours** = Non-RGA Administrative Work
- Prospect list creation, research, pre-call planning
- CRM updates, proposals, presentations, contracts
- Social selling, email templates, admin
- Schedule for early morning before Golden Hours or after 6 PM

### Power Hours: The Execution Framework

Schedule 3 Power Hours across the day -- morning, midday, and afternoon. During each:

- Do NOTHING but make prospecting calls
- Stay off email
- Remove ALL distractions (notifications off, door closed)
- Phone only, no multitasking
- 25-50 calls per hour target

**Horstman's Corollary:** Work contracts to fit time constraints. Challenge yourself: complete 10 prospecting calls in 30 minutes instead of spreading across hours. Time-bounded tasks force efficiency.

**The CEO Mindset:** Treat yourself as CEO of your territory. Calculate your hourly earnings value. Delegate tasks below your pay grade. Protect your prime selling time like it is money -- because it is.

> **BR-PT B2B Context:** In Brazil, Golden Hours for B2B services (clinics, offices, professionals) are typically 9:00-11:00 and 14:00-16:00. Avoid lunch (12:00-14:00). WhatsApp is the primary channel, not phone calls. Adapt Power Hours to WhatsApp + Phone combined blocks.

---

## 2. THE 30-DAY RULE -- PIPELINE MATHEMATICS

### The Core Principle

> "The prospecting you do in any 30-day period will pay off for the next 90 days."

This is the most important mathematical rule in sales. It is universal, and you ignore it at your peril.

### The Consequences Ladder

| What You Miss | What Happens |
|---|---|
| Miss 1 day of prospecting | It will bite you somewhere in the next 90 days |
| Miss 1 week | You will feel it in your commission check |
| Miss 1 month | You tank your pipeline, fall into a slump, and wake up 90 days later desperate, with no idea how you got there |

### Pipeline Math Example

```
Close Rate: 10%
Deals needed per month: 5
Pipeline required: 50 qualified opportunities
New prospects needed per month: 50+ (to replace closed + lost)

If you stop prospecting for 30 days:
- Day 1-30: Pipeline looks fine (you're closing prior prospects)
- Day 31-60: Pipeline starts thinning
- Day 61-90: CRISIS -- empty pipeline, no revenue, desperation mode
```

### The Slump Anatomy

Sales slumps are NOT closing problems. They are prospecting problems that happened 90 days ago.

```
MONTH 1: Heavy closing activity, light prospecting ("I'm too busy closing!")
MONTH 2: Fewer deals to close, but still coasting
MONTH 3: Pipeline is EMPTY. Panic mode. Desperate prospecting begins.
MONTH 4-6: Recovery (if disciplined -- takes 90 more days)
```

**The Fix:** NEVER stop prospecting regardless of how busy you are closing deals. Block prospecting time FIRST, close deals SECOND.

### Key Metrics to Track

- Total contacts made per day/week
- Appointments scheduled
- Calls-to-appointments ratio
- Appointments-to-proposals ratio
- Proposals-to-deals ratio
- Pipeline velocity (speed from prospect to close)
- Activity efficiency (volume generated per time block)

> **BR-PT B2B Context:** For Syra Digital's model (agency services), the sales cycle is typically 2-4 weeks for standard clients, 4-8 weeks for premium. The 30-Day Rule still applies: if Eric stops prospecting for 30 days, he will have no new leads in 60-90 days. With R$15k-30k average contract values, even 2-3 missing clients devastates monthly revenue.

---

## 3. THE 5-STEP TELEPHONE PROSPECTING FRAMEWORK

### The Framework

Blount's phone framework is designed to be fast, confident, and direct. The entire opening should take 15-25 seconds.

**Step 1: GET THEIR ATTENTION (Use Their Name)**
```
"Hi, Julie."
```
- Use their first name in a warm, confident tone
- Do NOT say "How are you today?" -- this gives them a chance to interrupt and derail your flow
- Do NOT ask permission ("Is this a good time?") -- it invites a brush-off

**Step 2: IDENTIFY YOURSELF**
```
"This is Jeb Blount with Sales Gravy."
```
- State your name and company transparently
- This reduces stress and builds credibility
- Being upfront about who you are makes you sound professional, not sneaky

**Step 3: TELL THEM WHY YOU ARE CALLING ("The Reason I'm Calling...")**
```
"The reason I am calling is to schedule an appointment with you..."
```
- Dive right in. Demonstrates professionalism
- Use the exact phrase "the reason I am calling" -- it is a pattern interrupt that signals transparency

**Step 4: BUILD A BRIDGE (The "Because" Statement)**
```
"...because many of my clients are frustrated that it takes too long
to get new salespeople ramped up to full productivity. Our software
typically cuts onboarding time by 50%..."
```
- Connect YOUR solution to THEIR pain
- Use emotional language: "frustrated," "worried," "struggling"
- Use proof: "saves," "cuts costs by," "our clients typically..."
- The word "because" is psychologically powerful -- it justifies the request

**Step 5: ASK FOR WHAT YOU WANT (Then Shut Up)**
```
"I'd like to schedule a brief 20-minute meeting to explore whether
this might be a fit. How does Wednesday at 3 PM work for you?"
```
- Be specific: suggest a day and time
- Be assumptive: "How does Wednesday work?" not "Would you be interested?"
- Then SHUT UP. Do not fill the silence. Let them respond
- Be ready to ask up to 3 times (three RBO turnarounds before gracefully exiting)

### Complete Script Example #1 (B2B SaaS)

```
"Hi Candace, this is Jeb Blount from Sales Gravy. The reason I am
calling is to schedule an appointment with you to show you our new
sales onboarding automation software. Many of my clients are frustrated
because it takes too long to get new salespeople ramped up to full
productivity and find that it's holding their business growth back.
Our software typically cuts onboarding time and costs for new sales
reps by 50 percent, and makes it super easy to manage new rep
onboarding, giving you the peace of mind that your new hires will
start selling fast. I'd love to schedule a brief meeting to see if
this might work for you. How does Tuesday afternoon look?"
```

### Complete Script Example #2 (B2B Services -- Contextualized)

```
"Hi Rick, this is Jeb with Acme Kitchen Supplies. The reason I am
calling is because I read in the paper you are building a restaurant
over on the 44 bypass. I wanted to learn more about your process for
purchasing kitchen equipment supplies. I know I am calling early in
the game. However, I found that when we get our design team working
with your team before you make critical decisions about kitchen
layout, you'll have more options in layout. You can often save a ton
of money in construction costs and future labor costs with a more
efficient and streamlined kitchen. Can you tell me how you make those
decisions and when the selection process will begin?"
```

### Key Principles

- **No pauses during the framework.** The moment you pause, you lose control
- **Speed matters.** Make calls quick and to the point
- **Transparency reduces resistance.** Being truthful about who you are and why you are calling reduces their stress
- **Emotional language:** Use words like "frustrated," "concerned," "save," "flexibility," "options," "time," "money"
- **Get to yes, no, or maybe as fast as possible.** Minimize time in uncertainty

> **BR-PT B2B Context (Syra Digital adaptation):**

```
"Oi Dr. [Nome], aqui e o Eric da Syra Digital. O motivo da minha
ligacao e que eu vi que o senhor tem uma clinica de [especialidade]
no Instagram e notei que o senhor tem muito potencial pra atrair
mais pacientes pelo digital. A maioria dos medicos que a gente
atende estava frustrada porque investia em marketing e nao via
retorno real em agenda. Nossos clientes tipicamente triplicam o
volume de agendamentos nos primeiros 90 dias. Gostaria de agendar
uma conversa rapida de 15 minutos pra ver se faz sentido pro senhor.
Quarta as 15h funciona?"
```

---

## 4. SOCIAL SELLING FRAMEWORK (5 C's)

### Jeb Blount's Position on Social Selling

Blount is explicitly clear: **Social selling alone will NEVER be enough to fill the pipeline.** It is a supplement, not a replacement for traditional prospecting.

> "Savvy sales professionals balance prospecting across multiple channels including phone, email, text, in-person, networking, and social. Contact and conversion rates via phone, email, and even text messaging DWARF conversion rates on social media."

### What Social Selling DOES Well

- Builds familiarity over time (Law of Familiarity)
- Provides prospect research and intelligence
- Helps build personal brand
- Facilitates warm introductions and referrals
- Creates awareness of trigger events

### What Social Selling Does NOT Do

- Close deals (conversion rates far lower than phone/email)
- Replace traditional prospecting
- Work as a standalone strategy
- Work if you pitch directly in DMs without context

### The 5 C's of Social Selling

1. **Connecting** -- Build a network of relevant connections. Connect with prospects, influencers, and industry peers. Quality over quantity, but volume matters.

2. **Content Creation** -- Create thought leadership posts, articles, ebooks, insights. Position yourself as an expert. Share your knowledge generously.

3. **Content Curation** -- Share relevant industry information, articles, news. Add your commentary. Show you are plugged in to the industry.

4. **Conversion** -- Drive direct engagement. Move social interactions toward real conversations (phone, video, meeting). Social is the START, not the end.

5. **Consistency** -- Regular, persistent activity. Daily engagement. Comment, like, share, post. Consistency builds familiarity. Sporadic activity is wasted activity.

### Required Tools

- Engagement platforms (LinkedIn, Instagram)
- Content creation tools
- Content curation resources
- Distribution channels
- Intelligence/data sources

### The LinkedIn Edge (2025 -- Latest Framework)

Blount's newest book, co-authored with Brynne Tillman, teaches:

- Using LinkedIn + AI to build better, more effective prospecting lists
- Integrating LinkedIn into outbound prospecting sequences to increase engagement
- Finding decision-makers using smart targeting strategies
- Using AI tools to streamline research and get crucial contact information
- Writing prospecting messages that convert with proven frameworks
- Blending fast outbound prospecting with systematic long-game relationship building
- Lowering resistance through relevance, consistency, and confidence

> **BR-PT B2B Context:** In Brazil, Instagram is more powerful than LinkedIn for B2B medical/aesthetic services. Apply the 5 C's to Instagram: (1) Connect with local doctors/clinic owners, (2) Create educational content about marketing results, (3) Curate industry news and cases, (4) Convert DM conversations to WhatsApp calls, (5) Post/engage consistently. WhatsApp replaces LinkedIn InMail as the primary messaging channel.

---

## 5. EMAIL PROSPECTING (4-Step HRBA Framework)

### The Framework: Hook / Relate / Bridge / Ask

**Step 1: HOOK -- Subject Line & Opening**

Subject line rules:
- Keep it SHORT: 3-6 words maximum
- Do NOT use questions as subject lines
- Use action words and directive statements
- Reference referrals or specific actions
- List-based subject lines are powerful
- Testimonial-based subject lines convert well

Effective subject line examples:
```
"Quick question about [company]"
"Idea for [their specific challenge]"
"[Mutual connection] suggested I reach out"
"3 ways to [solve their pain]"
"Saw your [trigger event]"
```

BAD subject lines (trigger delete reflex):
```
"Following up" (generic)
"Can I have 15 minutes?" (asks before giving value)
"Introducing [your company]" (nobody cares)
"RE: RE: RE:" (fake thread manipulation)
```

**Step 2: RELATE -- Demonstrate Understanding**

Show you understand their world, their challenges, their emotions.

```
"I know that managing a growing clinic while trying to attract
new patients through digital marketing can feel overwhelming,
especially when you've tried agencies before and didn't see
real results..."
```

People make decisions based on emotions. They respond when they feel UNDERSTOOD.

**Step 3: BRIDGE -- Connect Their Problem to Your Solution**

Give a concrete reason why YOU can help THEM.

```
"That's exactly why we built a system specifically for medical
clinics. Our clients typically see a 3x increase in qualified
patient inquiries within 90 days, without the doctor having to
spend any time on marketing."
```

Most people are motivated by selfish considerations. Answer "What's in it for ME?"

**Step 4: ASK -- Clear Call to Action**

```
"I'm not sure if this is a fit, but a quick 15-minute call would
tell us both. Would Thursday at 2 PM or Friday at 10 AM work
better for you?"
```

- Provide TWO specific time options
- Use "I'm not sure if this is a fit" to reduce pressure
- Make it easy for them to say yes

### Email Deliverability Rules

- Avoid images and hyperlinks in cold emails (spam triggers)
- Do NOT email multiple contacts at the same company simultaneously
- Schedule sends for off-hours so emails land during Golden Hours
- Personalize with name and company
- Keep the email SHORT -- under 100 words if possible
- Proofread before sending (always)

### Email Effectiveness

> Jeb Blount states that email is one of the most effective ways to SCALE prospecting -- if done right, it can be up to 20x more effective than other channels.

### Complete Email Template (B2B Services)

```
Subject: Idea for [Company Name]

Hi [First Name],

I noticed [trigger event / observation about their business].

Most [their role/industry] I speak with are frustrated because
[common pain point] and find that [consequence of pain].

We've helped [similar companies] achieve [specific result] by
[brief solution description].

I'm not sure if this would be relevant for you, but would you
have 15 minutes this week to explore? How does [Day] at [Time]
work?

Best,
[Your name]
[Company]
[Phone]
```

> **BR-PT B2B Context:** Email is less effective in Brazil than WhatsApp for initial outreach to medical professionals. However, email works well as a FOLLOW-UP channel after initial WhatsApp or phone contact. Use the HRBA framework in WhatsApp messages instead, keeping them even shorter (40-60 words). Subject lines become the first line of the WhatsApp message.

---

## 6. TEXT / WHATSAPP PROSPECTING (7-Step Framework)

### Core Principle

Text messaging works best as an INTEGRATED part of a larger prospecting system, NOT a standalone channel. The probability of your text converting increases exponentially when sent AFTER prior contact through another channel.

**Critical Statistic:** According to the Lead360 study (3.5 million lead records, 400+ companies):
- Text message alone: **4.8% conversion**
- Text AFTER phone contact: **conversion increases by 112.6%**

### The 7 Keys to Text Message Prospecting

1. **Use AFTER Other Channels** -- Text after a phone call, voicemail, email, networking event, or trigger event. Never text cold with zero prior contact.

2. **Identify Yourself** -- Always state who you are immediately. Anonymous texts get deleted or flagged as spam.

3. **Be Direct and Brief** -- Get to the point in 1-3 sentences. Respect the medium. Text is for short, punchy messages, not paragraphs.

4. **Maintain Proper Tone** -- Professional but conversational. Not too formal, not too casual. Match the prospect's communication style when possible.

5. **Avoid Abbreviations** -- Write complete words. "U" instead of "You" looks unprofessional in B2B context.

6. **Use Transparent, Full Links** -- If including links, use full URLs, not shortened/masked links (which look suspicious).

7. **Time it Right** -- Send at events, after trigger events, after phone attempts. Tuesday-Thursday mornings typically get best response rates.

### WhatsApp/Text Message Templates

**After Missed Call:**
```
"Oi [Nome], aqui e o Eric da Syra Digital. Tentei te ligar agora
ha pouco. Vi que voce tem uma clinica incrivel e queria trocar uma
ideia rapida sobre como triplicar seus agendamentos pelo digital.
Posso te ligar amanha as [hora]?"
```

**After Networking/Event:**
```
"Hi [Name], great meeting you at [event] yesterday. I'd love to
continue our conversation about [topic discussed]. Would you have
15 minutes this week for a quick call? I have some ideas that could
help with [their challenge]."
```

**Follow-Up After Email:**
```
"Hi [Name], I sent you an email earlier this week about [topic].
Just wanted to make sure it didn't get lost. Would a quick call
Thursday work?"
```

**Trigger Event Text:**
```
"Hi [Name], congratulations on [trigger event -- new location,
award, hiring, etc.]. I work with [similar companies] on [your
specialty]. Would love 15 minutes to share some ideas. Free
this week?"
```

> **BR-PT B2B Context:** WhatsApp IS the primary prospecting channel in Brazil. Blount's text framework maps directly to WhatsApp. Key adaptation: audio messages (voice notes) are more personal than text in Brazilian WhatsApp culture. Send a short voice note (15-30 seconds) referencing their name, what you noticed about their business, and a specific question. This combines the intimacy of phone with the convenience of text.

---

## 7. OBJECTIONS FRAMEWORK -- THE COMPLETE SYSTEM

### The Four Types of Objections

Blount categorizes ALL objections into four types, each requiring a different turnaround framework:

#### Type 1: PROSPECTING OBJECTIONS (RBOs -- Reflex Buyer Objections)

- Occur during cold outreach
- Harsh, automatic, reflexive
- Three subtypes: **Reflex Responses** ("Leave me alone"), **Brush-Offs** ("Send me some info"), **True Objections** (legitimate business reasons)
- Turnaround: **Ledge-Disrupt-Ask (LDA)**

#### Type 2: RED HERRINGS

- Irrelevant topics introduced to distract from the sales conversation
- Examples: "We're already talking to your competitor," random tangents
- Turnaround: **PAIS (Pause-Acknowledge-Ignore-Save)**

#### Type 3: MICRO-COMMITMENT OBJECTIONS

- Resistance to small progressive commitments (next steps, demos, meetings)
- Rarely harsh; more like brush-offs
- Turnaround: **Ledge-Explain Value-Ask**

#### Type 4: BUYING COMMITMENT OBJECTIONS

- Final-stage resistance to making a purchase decision
- The "sexy" objections: price, timing, competitor, need to think about it
- Turnaround: **Five-Step Framework (Relate-Isolate/Clarify-Minimize-Ask-Fallback)**

### The Turnaround Frameworks in Detail

#### FRAMEWORK 1: LDA (Ledge-Disrupt-Ask) -- For Prospecting Objections

**LEDGE** -- A memorized automatic response that gives your logical brain time to catch up with your emotions. It does NOT require thinking.

Ledge examples:
```
"That makes sense."
"I figured you might say that."
"I get that."
"I understand."
"That's fair."
```

**DISRUPT** -- A statement or question that breaks the prospect's expected pattern and pulls them toward you. They expect you to hang up or argue. Instead, you surprise them.

Disrupt examples:
```
"Most people aren't interested the first time I call, and that's
exactly why we should meet."

"Awesome. If you're getting great prices and service, you should
never think about changing. I'd just like to learn more about
your situation."

"That's exactly why I called -- I figured you would be [busy],
and I want to find a time that's more convenient for you."
```

**ASK** -- Ask for the meeting AGAIN. Directly. Confidently. Assumptively. Without hesitation.

```
"How about we grab 15 minutes next Tuesday to see if there's
even a fit?"
```

**Rule:** You get up to 3 attempts (Ledge-Disrupt-Ask cycles) before gracefully exiting. Most salespeople give up after the first objection. Ultra-high performers ask at least twice.

#### FRAMEWORK 2: PAIS -- For Red Herrings

**P -- Pause:** Collect your emotions. Don't react.

**A -- Acknowledge:** Show you heard them. Take notes. "That's interesting, I've noted that."

**I -- Ignore:** Don't chase the distraction. Don't engage with it.

**S -- Save:** If the prospect brings it up again, address it at a more appropriate time.

Then redirect with an open-ended question to regain control of the conversation.

#### FRAMEWORK 3: Ledge-Explain Value-Ask -- For Micro-Commitment Objections

**LEDGE:** 
```
"That's exactly why I asked."
```

**EXPLAIN VALUE (WIIFM -- What's In It For Me?):**
- Emotional value (how they'll FEEL)
- Insight value (what they'll LEARN)
- Tangible value (what they'll GET -- data, savings, proof)

**ASK:** Request the commitment again.

Example:
```
Prospect: "My calendar is really full, so just call me next week."

You: "I've got a packed schedule next week too. Why don't we book
now so neither of us has to remember? How about Wednesday at 2:30?"
```

**Golden Rule:** Never leave a conversation without a firm next step with a specific date and time.

#### FRAMEWORK 4: Five-Step Turnaround -- For Buying Commitment Objections

**Step 1: RELATE** -- Empathy without judgment.
```
"I understand how you feel."
"That makes complete sense."
"I get why you'd want to think about that."
```
DO NOT argue. DO NOT dismiss. DO NOT say "but..."

**Step 2: ISOLATE & CLARIFY** -- Find the real objection.
- Isolate: "Other than this, is there anything else that's concerning you?"
- Clarify: "Help me understand -- what specifically about the price concerns you?"
- Use open-ended questions to dig deeper

**Step 3: MINIMIZE** -- Reduce the emotional size of the objection while maximizing the value of your proposal.
- Remind them of their PAIN (why they started this conversation)
- Remind them of what they've already AGREED TO (prior yeses)
- Paint the FUTURE STATE (what life looks like with your solution)
- Reference their prior COMMITMENTS (micro-commitments collected)

**Step 4: ASK** -- Request the commitment again. Confidently. Assumptively.
```
"Based on everything we've discussed, I think it makes sense to
move forward. Shall we get the paperwork started?"
```

**Step 5: FALLBACK** -- If the ask fails, have pre-planned alternatives:
- A smaller initial commitment
- A pilot/trial period
- A demo expansion
- A follow-up meeting with additional stakeholders
- A reduced scope

> **BR-PT B2B Context:** Brazilian prospects are culturally more indirect with objections. "Vou pensar" (I'll think about it) is the most common buying objection. It almost never means they're actually thinking. Apply the Five-Step Framework: Relate ("Faz total sentido"), Isolate ("Alem disso, tem mais alguma duvida?"), Minimize (remind of pain and agreed benefits), Ask again, Fallback to a smaller commitment.

---

## 8. REFLEX RESPONSES -- HANDLING KNEE-JERK OBJECTIONS

### What Are Reflex Responses?

Reflex Responses (part of RBOs) are automatic, unconscious defensive reactions. The prospect is NOT actually thinking about what they are saying. They are running on autopilot. They have been conditioned by hundreds of prospecting calls to fire off these responses instantly.

### The Most Common Reflex Responses and Turnarounds

#### "I'm busy right now."

```
LEDGE: "I figured you would be."
DISRUPT: "That's exactly why I called -- I want to find a time 
that works better for you."
ASK: "How about Thursday at 2 PM?"
```

#### "I'm not interested."

```
LEDGE: "That makes sense."
DISRUPT: "Most people aren't the first time I call, and that's 
exactly why we should meet."
ASK: "All I need is 15 minutes. How does Tuesday look?"
```

Alternative disruption:
```
"You know, that's exactly what a lot of my current clients said 
the first time I called. Most people aren't interested before 
they see how much we can help. I don't know if I'm a good fit 
for you, but doesn't it make sense to at least get together for 
a short meeting to find out?"
```

#### "Just send me some information."

```
LEDGE: "I'd be happy to."
DISRUPT: "I've got a lot of information I could send. So I send 
you the right thing, can I ask you a couple of quick questions?"
ASK: [Ask qualifying questions, THEN book the meeting]
```

Alternative:
```
"I'd love to. But honestly, the best information I can give you 
is specific to YOUR situation, and I'd need about 15 minutes to 
understand that. How about we do a quick call Thursday and then 
I can put together something really relevant for you?"
```

#### "We already have a provider / We're all set."

```
LEDGE: "Awesome."
DISRUPT: "If you're getting great prices and service, you should 
never think about changing. All I want is a few minutes of your 
time to learn more about you and see if we're even a fit. Even if 
we're not, I'll send you a competitive comparison that keeps your 
current provider honest."
ASK: "How does Friday at 10 work?"
```

#### "Call me back in 6 months."

```
LEDGE: "I will definitely do that."
DISRUPT: "In the meantime, I'd love to learn a bit more about 
your situation so when I call back, I can bring something really 
relevant. Can I ask you a couple of quick questions?"
ASK: [Qualify, then try to schedule a closer follow-up]
```

#### "I'm in a meeting right now."

```
LEDGE: "I apologize for the interruption."
DISRUPT: "I'll be really quick -- just 30 seconds."
ASK: "I'm calling to schedule a brief meeting. When would be a 
better time to chat -- tomorrow morning or Thursday afternoon?"
```

### The Master Psychology

The person in the conversation who exerts the greatest amount of **emotional control** has the highest probability of getting the outcome they desire. Reflex responses are designed to trigger YOUR emotional reaction (embarrassment, fear, retreat). When you respond with calm confidence and a prepared turnaround, you break the pattern and regain control.

> **BR-PT B2B Context:** The Brazilian equivalent reflex responses are: "Me manda no WhatsApp" (send it on WhatsApp), "Agora nao da" (can't right now), "Ja tenho agencia" (I already have an agency), "Vou falar com meu socio" (I need to talk to my partner). The same LDA framework applies. Key: always sound casual and confident, never pushy. Brazilian culture penalizes aggression in sales.

---

## 9. MICRO-COMMITMENTS -- THE LADDER TO YES

### Core Concept

Micro-commitments are small, low-risk, easy-to-consume steps in the sales process. After collecting enough micro-commitments, the final close feels like a natural, inevitable next step -- not a big, scary decision.

### Why Micro-Commitments Matter

> "The number one reason why deals stall is the failure to get to the next step." -- Jeb Blount

Asking for and getting micro-commitments consistently accelerates pipeline velocity.

### The Commitment Ladder

```
COMMITMENT #1: "Can I ask you a couple of quick questions?"
     |
COMMITMENT #2: Prospect agrees to meeting time
     |
COMMITMENT #3: "Let me grab your email and send you a calendar invite."
     |
COMMITMENT #4: Prospect confirms attendance (email reply or verbal)
     |
COMMITMENT #5: Shows up to the meeting
     |
COMMITMENT #6: Agrees to share their situation/challenges
     |
COMMITMENT #7: Agrees to a follow-up meeting / demo
     |
COMMITMENT #8: Brings decision-maker to next meeting
     |
COMMITMENT #9: Reviews proposal
     |
COMMITMENT #10: Agrees to move forward (THE CLOSE)
```

### Building the Ladder in Practice

When your prospect agrees to meet, ALWAYS repeat it back to them:

```
"Great, so we're set for Wednesday at 3 PM."
```

When they say YES, that is **Commitment #1**.

Then say:

```
"Let me grab your email and I'll send you a meeting invite for 
your calendar, just to make it convenient for you."
```

That gets another YES. That is **Commitment #2**.

### Key Techniques

1. **Never leave a conversation without a firm next step** with a specific date, time, and mutual commitment
2. **Frame commitments as low-risk:** "Just a quick 15-minute call to see if there's even a fit"
3. **Stack yeses progressively:** Each yes makes the next yes easier
4. **Remind them of prior agreements:** When facing buying objections, list all the things they already said yes to
5. **Minimize the emotional size of the ask** while maximizing the value of what they get

### The Psychological Mechanism

Once someone says yes to a small request, they are psychologically compelled to remain consistent with that commitment (Cialdini's Commitment & Consistency principle). Each micro-commitment creates a psychological anchor that pulls them toward the final close.

> **BR-PT B2B Context:** In Brazilian B2B, the micro-commitment ladder often includes WhatsApp-specific steps: (1) They reply to your WhatsApp, (2) They agree to receive a short video/audio, (3) They ask a question back, (4) They agree to a call, (5) They show up. Each step is a commitment. Sending a case study PDF or a 60-second results video via WhatsApp is a powerful micro-commitment ask.

---

## 10. SALES EQ -- EMOTIONAL INTELLIGENCE IN SALES

### The Core Thesis

> "Sales-specific emotional intelligence (Sales EQ) is MORE essential to success than education, experience, industry awareness, product knowledge, skills, or raw IQ."

> "The emotional experience of buying from you is far more important than products, prices, features, and solutions."

### Dual Process Theory in Sales

Contrary to popular belief, people act on EMOTION and justify their decisions after the fact with LOGIC.

```
WRONG assumption: Prospect evaluates features → compares prices → makes rational decision
ACTUAL behavior: Prospect FEELS something → makes emotional decision → finds logical justification
```

This means: The way you make someone FEEL during the sales process is more important than your slides, your data, or your pricing.

### The Four Pillars of Sales-Specific Emotional Intelligence

#### Pillar 1: EMPATHY

Ultra-high performers believe their primary mission is to SERVE their customers. Their mindset is others-focused. Because of this, they view things from the buyer's perspective -- both rationally and emotionally. This enables them to adjust their behavioral and communication style to make the client comfortable.

**In Practice:**
- Ask about THEIR situation before pitching
- Mirror their communication style
- Acknowledge their frustrations genuinely
- Listen more than you speak (the 80/20 rule)

#### Pillar 2: SELF-AWARENESS

Ultra-high performers are NOT perfect. They have the same weaknesses as anyone else. What sets them apart is a KEEN AWARENESS of their strengths and weaknesses. This awareness allows them to more effectively interact with others.

**In Practice:**
- Know your emotional triggers (what makes you defensive, eager, desperate)
- Recognize when disruptive emotions are taking over
- Understand your communication strengths and blind spots
- Seek feedback and honestly assess your performance

#### Pillar 3: SELF-CONTROL (Managing Disruptive Emotions)

Self-control is the ability to control disruptive emotions. This is what sets ultra-high performers apart from average salespeople.

**The 7 Disruptive Emotions:**

| Emotion | Impact | Management |
|---|---|---|
| **FEAR** | Root cause of most sales failures. Causes hesitation, excuse-making, avoidance of asks | Build exposure gradually. Track successes. Fear fades with action |
| **DESPERATION** | Makes you needy, weak, illogical. Instantly unlikeable | Keep pipeline full. Focus on serving, not closing. Detach from outcomes |
| **INSECURITY** | Drowns confidence. "Only I have a sign on my back that says reject me" | Reframe rejection as normal business. Track wins, not losses |
| **NEED FOR SIGNIFICANCE** | Ego drives fight-or-flight. Prioritizes looking good over results | Decouple self-worth from individual outcomes. Focus on process |
| **ATTACHMENT** | Losing perspective, objectivity. Delusional about deals | Focus on process, not outcomes. Set clear qualification criteria |
| **EAGERNESS** | Over-accommodation. Giving in too soon on price/terms | Establish value before negotiating. Remember mutual benefit |
| **WORRY** | Analysis paralysis. Focus on what could go wrong instead of right | Visualize positive outcomes. Use decision frameworks |

#### Pillar 4: SALES DRIVE (Relationship Management)

Sales is an emotional rollercoaster. Ultra-high performers master maintaining high performance in constant change. They combine intrinsic motivation with the discipline to execute consistently regardless of emotional state.

### The Five Stakeholders You Meet in a Deal (BASIC Model)

1. **Buyers** -- Decision makers with yes/no authority
2. **Amplifiers** -- Problem identifiers aligned with your solutions
3. **Seekers** -- Information gatherers evaluating options
4. **Influencers** -- Active process participants (advocates, naysayers, or agnostic)
5. **Coaches** -- Insider advocates who provide strategic intelligence

**Strategy:** Map every deal to identify all stakeholders. Build relationships with each type. Coaches are your most valuable allies -- cultivate them.

### The Prospect Self-Disclosure Loop (5 Steps)

1. Begin with open-ended questions
2. Provide complete attention and active listening
3. Avoid interrupting or rushing
4. Pause 3-5 seconds before speaking
5. Center follow-up questions on what they just disclosed

This loop creates trust and makes the prospect feel understood, which is the foundation of Sales EQ.

> **BR-PT B2B Context:** Brazilian business culture is heavily relationship-driven. Sales EQ matters even MORE here than in the US. The emotional connection often matters more than the rational argument. Building rapport ("construir relacionamento") through genuine interest in the doctor's practice, family, challenges, and goals is not "waste of time" -- it IS the sales process. The doctor who trusts you will pay your price. The doctor who doesn't trust you won't buy at any price.

---

## 11. ULTRA-HIGH PERFORMANCE -- PRODUCTIVITY & DISCIPLINE

### The "Eat the Frog" Principle

> "If it's your job to eat a frog, it's best to do it first thing in the morning. And if it's your job to eat two frogs, eat the biggest one first."

The frog is PROSPECTING. Do it FIRST. Before email. Before meetings. Before anything else.

### The Daily Schedule of an Ultra-High Performer

```
06:00-07:00  Morning routine, exercise, preparation
07:00-08:00  Platinum Hours: list building, research, CRM updates
08:00-10:00  POWER HOUR #1 (Golden Hours): Phone prospecting block
10:00-10:15  Break + reward
10:15-11:00  Email prospecting + social selling
11:00-12:00  Client meetings / demos / presentations
12:00-13:00  Lunch + networking
13:00-14:00  POWER HOUR #2: Phone prospecting block
14:00-16:00  Client meetings / proposals / follow-ups
16:00-17:00  POWER HOUR #3: Phone prospecting + voicemails
17:00-17:30  CRM updates, next-day prep, admin
17:30        "One more call" before leaving
```

### High-Intensity Prospecting Sprints

Blount is a fan of short bursts of maximum intensity:

- Carve out **10-15 minutes**
- Chop wood as FAST as you can (rapid-fire calls)
- Take a short break
- Sprint again

This keeps energy up and prevents the mental fatigue of long, dragging prospecting sessions.

### The Work Compression Model

Based on Parkinson's Law (work expands to fill time available) and Horstman's Corollary (work contracts into time allowed):

```
INEFFICIENT: "I'll make calls all morning" → 20 calls in 3 hours
COMPRESSED: "I'll make 20 calls in the next 45 minutes" → Done
```

Set aggressive time boundaries. Use a timer. Race yourself.

### Mental Toughness Development (Athletic Model)

1. **Self-confidence through preparation** -- Know your scripts, know your value, know your numbers
2. **Attention control** -- Minimize negative energy, maximize positive
3. **Motivation maintenance** -- Daily reminders of WHY you sell
4. **Attitude control** -- Choose your emotional state every morning
5. **Visualization** -- Pre-program success by mentally rehearsing calls, focusing on breathing, imagining confident responses

### Grit Development Questions

Write and answer these:
1. What do I want?
2. How badly do I want it?
3. How will I achieve it?

### Continuous Improvement ("Sharpen the Saw")

- Listen to audiobooks/podcasts while driving
- Regular exercise (non-negotiable)
- Adequate sleep
- Healthy eating
- Weekly skill development
- **"Continuous learning = continuous earning"**

### The Ultimate Principle

> "When it's time to go home, make one more call."

The extra effort compounds. The person who makes one more call per day makes 250+ more calls per year. That is 25+ additional appointments, which is 5-10 additional deals, which could be tens of thousands in additional revenue.

> **BR-PT B2B Context:** For Eric at Syra Digital, the "frog" is prospecting DMs and calls to new doctors. The natural temptation is to focus on servicing existing clients (reactive). The discipline is to block 1 hour EVERY DAY for pure outbound prospecting before anything else. Use the sprint method: 15-minute bursts of WhatsApp outreach, then 15 minutes of phone calls, then break. This is sustainable and prevents burnout.

---

## 12. TRIGGER EVENTS -- TIMING YOUR OUTREACH

### What Are Trigger Events?

Trigger events are changes in a prospect's situation that create an opening for your solution. They signal that the prospect may be entering a buying window.

### Types of Trigger Events

**Company-Level Triggers:**
- New office/location opening
- Mergers and acquisitions
- Leadership changes (new CEO, CMO, etc.)
- Funding rounds / new investment
- Expansion announcements
- Product launches
- Awards / recognition
- Regulatory changes affecting their industry
- Public earnings reports (positive or negative)

**Individual-Level Triggers:**
- New job / promotion
- Published article or interview
- Conference presentation
- Social media post about a challenge
- LinkedIn profile update
- Industry award

**Market-Level Triggers:**
- Industry regulation changes
- Competitive landscape shifts
- Technology disruptions
- Economic conditions
- Seasonal patterns

### Blount's Perspective on Timing

Critically, Blount advises AGAINST trying to "time" individual calls perfectly:

> "Forget about timing your calls and commit instead to a daily, first-thing-in-the-morning call block."

**The Logic:** Well-crafted prospecting SEQUENCES improve the statistical probability that you engage prospects at the right time, through the right channel, with the right message. You cannot predict the perfect moment, but you CAN be consistent enough that you are present when the window opens.

### Using Trigger Events in Practice

```
PHONE SCRIPT WITH TRIGGER EVENT:
"Hi Dr. [Name], this is Eric from Syra Digital. I noticed you 
just opened a second location on [street/area] -- congratulations! 
The reason I'm calling is that most doctors we work with found 
that launching digital marketing for a new location from day one 
cuts the time to a full schedule by about 60%. I'd love to share 
how we've done this for other clinics. Would a quick 15-minute 
call this week make sense?"
```

```
EMAIL WITH TRIGGER EVENT:
Subject: Congratulations on [trigger event]

Hi [Name],

Saw the news about [trigger event]. Exciting times!

When [similar companies] go through this transition, they 
typically face [specific challenge]. We've helped [number] 
companies in your space navigate this and [specific result].

Would you have 15 minutes this week to explore if we could 
help? [Day] at [Time]?
```

### Familiarity vs. Timing

> "It takes 20-50 touches to engage a cold prospect who has never heard of you."

Building familiarity is more important than perfect timing. If you have been consistently touching a prospect for months (email, social, voicemail), when a trigger event hits, they already know who you are. That is when the call converts.

> **BR-PT B2B Context:** Key trigger events for medical/aesthetic clinic prospects in Brazil: opening new clinic, hiring new staff, competitor launching heavy marketing, Instagram growth plateau, engagement drop, new procedure offering, published in medical journal, speaking at congress. Monitor Instagram, Google Alerts, and medical society publications. When a trigger event happens, reach out within 24-48 hours.

---

## 13. VOICEMAIL SCRIPTS -- THE 5-STEP FRAMEWORK

### The Rules

- Keep voicemails to **30 seconds** maximum
- Only leave voicemails for known/targeted prospects (not spray-and-pray)
- A voicemail's job is to get a CALLBACK, not to sell
- Use voicemails as part of a multi-touch sequence, not in isolation

### The 5-Step Voicemail Framework

**Step 1: Identify Yourself**
```
"Hi Rick, this is Jeb Blount from Sales Gravy."
```

**Step 2: Say Your Phone Number (Slowly, Twice)**
```
"My phone number is 1-888-360-2249. That's 1-888-360-2249."
```
Prospects cannot call back if they do not have or you garbled your number. Say it SLOWLY. Say it TWICE.

**Step 3: State Your Reason for Calling**
```
"The reason I'm calling is you downloaded our whitepaper on cold 
calling and I want to learn more about your situation and what 
triggered you to seek out this information."
```

**Step 4: Pique Curiosity (Create a Reason to Call Back)**
```
"I also have some additional resources on voicemail messages and 
phone prospecting I thought you might be curious to learn about."
```

**Step 5: Repeat Your Name and Number**
```
"Again, this is Jeb Blount, 1-888-360-2249."
```

### Complete Voicemail Script Example

```
"Hi Rick, this is Jeb Blount from Sales Gravy. My number is 
1-888-360-2249, that's 1-888-360-2249. The reason I'm calling 
is you downloaded our whitepaper on cold calling and I want to 
learn more about your situation and what triggered you to seek 
out this information. I also have some additional resources on 
phone prospecting I thought you'd be curious about. Again, this 
is Jeb Blount, 1-888-360-2249. I look forward to hearing from 
you."
```

**Total time: ~25 seconds**

### Voicemail Best Practices

- **Speak at a measured pace** -- Not too fast, not too slow
- **Sound confident and enthusiastic** -- Your tone matters more than your words
- **Practice your voicemail until it sounds natural** -- Not scripted
- **Do NOT worry about perfect timing** -- Consistency beats timing
- **Leave voicemail as PART of a sequence** -- Voicemail + email + social touch in the same day creates a surround-sound effect

> **BR-PT B2B Context:** In Brazil, voicemail is nearly dead. The equivalent is the **WhatsApp voice note (audio message)**. Apply Blount's 5-step framework to a 20-30 second WhatsApp audio: (1) Identify yourself, (2) State your phone number if relevant, (3) State why you're reaching out, (4) Create curiosity, (5) Close with next step. Audio messages feel MORE personal than text in Brazilian culture and have much higher listen/response rates.

---

## 14. VIDEO PROSPECTING

### Jeb Blount's Virtual Selling Framework

Blount's "Virtual Selling" book is the definitive guide to video-based prospecting. Key teaching:

### The Seven Technical Elements of Video Sales Calls

1. **Audio** -- Invest in a quality microphone. Reduce background noise and room echo. People tolerate bad video but NOT bad audio.

2. **Lighting** -- Face a window or place a professional ring light behind your camera at face level. Good lighting = trust and professionalism.

3. **Framing** -- Position yourself properly within the frame. Eyes at the top third. Some space above your head. Not too close, not too far.

4. **Backdrop** -- Use professional backgrounds: bookshelf, clean office, virtual background with client logo (for demos). Avoid distracting or messy environments.

5. **Internet Connection** -- Maximize upload speed. Have phone hotspot as backup. Nothing kills credibility faster than freezing/buffering.

6. **Platform Mastery** -- Invest in learning two videoconferencing platforms thoroughly. Be the expert, not the person fumbling with screen share.

7. **Camera Angle** -- Eye level or slightly above. Never looking up at the camera from below (unflattering and implies subservience).

### The Five Human Elements of Video Sales Calls

1. **Energy & Enthusiasm** -- Amplify your energy 20% more than in person. Video flattens energy.

2. **Eye Contact** -- Look at the CAMERA, not the screen. This creates the illusion of direct eye contact for the viewer.

3. **Body Language** -- Sit up straight. Use hand gestures (visible in frame). Lean slightly forward to show engagement.

4. **Vocal Variety** -- Vary pitch, pace, and volume. Monotone kills engagement on video faster than in person.

5. **Active Listening Cues** -- Nod visibly. React facially. Say "mmhm" and "I see" to show you are present and listening.

### Video Prospecting Message Framework

Apply the Hook/Relate/Bridge/Ask framework to video:

```
[15-30 second video message]

HOOK: "Hi [Name], I just noticed [something specific about them]."
RELATE: "Most [their role] I speak with are dealing with [pain]."
BRIDGE: "We've helped [similar companies] achieve [result]."
ASK: "I'd love 15 minutes to see if this could work for you.
I'll follow up with an email to make it easy to schedule."
```

### The Multi-Channel Video Sequence

1. Send a short personalized video via email (embed or link)
2. Leave a voicemail referencing the video to create curiosity
3. Send a follow-up email with the video link
4. Connect on social media and reference the video
5. Text/WhatsApp linking to the video

The video becomes the centerpiece of a multi-touch sequence. Each touch references and reinforces it.

### Overcoming Camera Fear

- Practice daily (record yourself, watch, improve)
- Start with internal team videos before sending to prospects
- Use a teleprompter app for your key talking points
- Remember: authenticity beats perfection
- A mediocre personalized video beats a perfect generic email every time

> **BR-PT B2B Context:** Video messages via WhatsApp (selfie-style, 30-60 seconds) are extremely powerful in Brazilian B2B. The doctor sees a real person talking directly to them. It cuts through the noise instantly. Record in a professional setting, mention their clinic by name, reference something specific about their Instagram, and ask for a quick call. This format combines Blount's video framework with WhatsApp's dominance in Brazil.

---

## 15. KEY SCRIPTS -- COMPLETE COLLECTION

### Opening Scripts (Phone)

**Generic B2B Opening:**
```
"Hi [Name], this is [Your name] from [Company]. The reason I'm 
calling is [specific reason tied to their situation]. [Bridge: 
because statement with value/pain]. Would it make sense to 
schedule a quick 15-minute call to explore this? How does 
[specific day and time] work?"
```

**Trigger Event Opening:**
```
"Hi [Name], this is [Your name] from [Company]. I noticed that 
[trigger event]. When companies go through [this change], they 
typically [face this challenge]. We've helped [X similar companies] 
[achieve this result]. I'd love to share how. Would [day] at 
[time] work for a brief call?"
```

**Referral Opening:**
```
"Hi [Name], [Mutual contact] suggested I reach out to you. They 
mentioned you might be dealing with [challenge] and thought I 
could help. We've worked with [mutual contact] on [result]. 
Would you have 15 minutes this week to see if there's a fit?"
```

**Inbound Lead Follow-Up:**
```
"Hi [Name], this is [Your name] from [Company]. You downloaded 
our [resource] on [topic] and I wanted to learn more about your 
situation and what triggered your interest. I also have some 
additional resources I think you'd find valuable. Do you have 
a few minutes now, or would [day] at [time] work better?"
```

### Bridge Scripts (The "Because" Connections)

**Pain-Based Bridge:**
```
"...because most [their role] I speak with are frustrated that 
[specific pain]. Our clients typically see [specific result] 
within [timeframe]..."
```

**Insight-Based Bridge:**
```
"...because I've been tracking [industry trend] and noticed that 
[insight]. I think there's an opportunity for you to [benefit]..."
```

**Social Proof Bridge:**
```
"...because we recently helped [similar company] achieve [result], 
and when I saw your situation, I thought the same approach might 
work for you..."
```

**Curiosity Bridge:**
```
"...because I have some ideas about [their challenge] that I 
haven't seen anyone else in your market implement yet..."
```

### Ask Scripts (Closing for the Meeting)

**Assumptive Ask:**
```
"I'd love to schedule a brief meeting to explore this. How does 
Wednesday at 3 PM work for you?"
```

**Alternative Ask:**
```
"Would Tuesday morning or Thursday afternoon work better for a 
quick 15-minute call?"
```

**Low-Pressure Ask:**
```
"I'm not sure if this is even a fit, but a quick call would tell 
us both. How about [day] at [time]?"
```

**Value-First Ask:**
```
"I've put together a quick analysis specifically for [their company] 
that I think you'd find interesting. Can I walk you through it in 
15 minutes? How does [day] work?"
```

### Objection Turnaround Scripts (Complete Set)

**"I'm busy."**
```
"I figured you would be -- that's exactly why I want to find a 
time that works for you. How about [day] at [time]?"
```

**"I'm not interested."**
```
"That makes sense. Most people aren't the first time I call. 
That's exactly why a brief meeting makes sense -- so you can 
see if it's worth being interested. [Day] at [time]?"
```

**"Send me some information."**
```
"I'd be happy to. So I can send you the most relevant information, 
can I ask a couple quick questions? [Qualify, then pivot to 
scheduling a call]"
```

**"We already have a provider."**
```
"Awesome. If you're getting great results, you should stick with 
them. All I'd like is 15 minutes to compare notes. Even if we're 
not a fit, I can give you a benchmark to keep your current 
provider honest. [Day] at [time]?"
```

**"Call me back in [timeframe]."**
```
"I absolutely will. In the meantime, can I ask what's happening 
in [timeframe] that makes it a better time? [Gather intelligence, 
then try to schedule something sooner]"
```

**"What's the price?"**
```
"Great question -- and it really depends on your specific 
situation. Every client is different. That's why a brief 
conversation would help me give you an accurate picture. 
How does [day] work?"
```

**"I need to think about it." (Buying Objection)**
```
"That makes complete sense. Just so I understand -- when you say 
you want to think about it, is it the [price / timing / scope] 
that's giving you pause, or something else? 
[Isolate → Clarify → Minimize → Ask again → Fallback]"
```

### The "Next" Card

Keep an index card at your desk that reads:

```
NEXT.
```

After every rejection, look at the card. Say "Next" out loud. Move on. The card is your emotional ledge -- it gives your brain the pause it needs to avoid spiraling into disruptive emotions after rejection.

> **BR-PT B2B Context -- Adapted Script Collection:**

```
WHATSAPP OPENING (Cold DM to Doctor):
"Oi Dr. [Nome], tudo bem? Aqui e o Eric da Syra Digital. Vi o 
perfil da sua clinica no Instagram e fiquei impressionado com 
[detalhe especifico -- trabalho, antes/depois, conteudo]. 
A maioria dos medicos que a gente atende estava frustrada 
porque investia em marketing digital e nao via pacientes reais 
na agenda. Nossos clientes tipicamente triplicam agendamentos 
em 90 dias. Sera que faz sentido bater um papo rapido de 15 
min? Pode ser por aqui mesmo ou por ligacao."

WHATSAPP FOLLOW-UP (After no reply, 3-5 days later):
"Dr. [Nome], mandei uma mensagem ha alguns dias. Sei como e 
corrido o dia a dia de clinica. So queria compartilhar um caso 
rapido: ajudamos a Dra. [Nome] a sair de [X] para [Y] 
agendamentos/mes em 90 dias. Se tiver curiosidade, e so me 
responder aqui."

WHATSAPP AUDIO (Voice note, 20-30 seconds):
"Oi Dr. [Nome], aqui e o Eric da Syra Digital. Vi que o senhor 
acabou de [trigger event]. Normalmente quando isso acontece, 
existe uma janela pra crescer muito rapido no digital. Queria 
trocar uma ideia rapida. Me responde aqui quando tiver um 
minutinho."
```

## 16. SALES GRAVY PODCAST -- KEY TEACHINGS

### About the Podcast

The Sales Gravy Podcast is the world's most listened-to sales podcast with over 29 million downloads. Hosted by Jeb Blount, featuring the "Ask Jeb" segment where he answers listener questions.

### Key Recurring Teachings

#### On Standing Out in a Noisy World

The tsunami of poorly written AI-generated outreach actually HELPS you stand out if your message is empathetic, clear, and focused on the prospect's key interests. Take time to step into their shoes and know their persona, industry, and how you solve their burning issues.

#### On Targeted vs. Spray & Pray

Focus on a list of prospects with something in common -- same industry, similar role, same geography. This allows targeted messaging that speaks to a collective pain point. Save fully personalized messaging for highest-value prospects (C-suite, major accounts).

#### On Building Multi-Touch Conversations

Each touch -- voicemail, email, text, social message -- should flow logically from the last. Do NOT:
- Leave the same voicemail three times in a row
- Send "Just bumping this to the top of your inbox" emails
- Copy-paste the same DM

Instead, let your communication BUILD A CASE for why a conversation is worthwhile. Each touch adds new information, new value, new reason.

#### On Handling No-Shows

Blount's system for preventing no-shows:
1. Confirm appointments verbally when scheduled
2. Send detailed calendar invites immediately
3. Record and send a personal video before the meeting
4. Leave an enthusiastic voicemail the day before
5. A/B test morning-of confirmation emails
6. Track no-show metrics after 30 days to analyze what works

#### On the "I Already Have a Solution" Objection

When prospects say they already have a provider, instead of arguing, **agree with them** and then pivot to the gap you fill:

```
"That's great that you have someone handling that. What I've found 
is that even when things are going well, having a fresh perspective 
can uncover opportunities your current provider might be missing. 
All I'm asking for is 15 minutes."
```

#### On Goal Setting

> "Real sales goals require a SYSTEM, not just motivation or inspiration."

Break annual goals into quarterly targets, monthly targets, weekly activities, and daily behaviors. Reverse-engineer from the number backwards:

```
Annual revenue goal: R$1,000,000
Average deal size: R$20,000
Deals needed: 50
Close rate: 20%
Proposals needed: 250
Meetings needed: 500
Calls needed: 5,000
Daily calls needed: ~20 (250 working days)
```

#### On Self-Awareness

> "Self-awareness is the ultimate sales skill. It is the real make-or-break factor."

The top 1% of salespeople are brutally honest with themselves about their weaknesses, their emotions, and their behaviors. They do not rationalize poor performance or blame external factors. They look inward first.

### Books by Jeb Blount (Complete Bibliography)

1. **Fanatical Prospecting** (2015) -- The prospecting bible
2. **Sales EQ** (2017) -- Emotional intelligence in sales
3. **Objections** (2018) -- Getting past no
4. **Inked** (2020) -- Sales negotiation
5. **Virtual Selling** (2020) -- Video/virtual sales
6. **Selling in a Crisis** (2022) -- Recession-proof selling
7. **Fanatical Prospecting Sequences** (2024) -- Multi-touch cadences
8. **The LinkedIn Edge** (2025) -- LinkedIn + AI prospecting
9. **The AI Edge** (2025) -- AI in sales

## SYNTHESIS: THE BLOUNT SYSTEM IN ONE PAGE

```
MINDSET:     Fanatical discipline + emotional intelligence
MATH:        30-Day Rule (prospect today → revenue in 90 days)
TIME:        Golden Hours (prospecting) + Platinum Hours (admin)
EXECUTION:   Power Hours (3x daily, phone/WhatsApp blocks)
CHANNELS:    Phone + Email + Text + Social + Video (balanced mix)
PHONE:       5-Step Framework (Attention → ID → Reason → Bridge → Ask)
EMAIL:       4-Step HRBA (Hook → Relate → Bridge → Ask)
TEXT:        After other channels, brief, professional, transparent
SOCIAL:      5 C's (Connect → Create → Curate → Convert → Consistency)
VIDEO:       7 Technical + 5 Human elements, personalized messages
VOICEMAIL:   30 seconds max, number twice, pique curiosity
OBJECTIONS:  4 types, each with specific turnaround framework
PROSPECTING: Ledge-Disrupt-Ask (up to 3 attempts)
RED HERRING: PAIS (Pause-Acknowledge-Ignore-Save)
MICRO-COMMIT: Ledge-Explain Value-Ask
BUYING:      Relate-Isolate/Clarify-Minimize-Ask-Fallback
EMOTIONS:    Manage 7 disruptive emotions through self-awareness
PIPELINE:    Never stop prospecting. The full pipeline is the goal.
CLOSE:       Stack micro-commitments → close becomes inevitable
GROWTH:      Continuous learning. One more call. Sharpen the saw.
```

# Predictable Revenue & Modern SDR/Outbound Sales: Complete Research Document
