## 1. Predictable Revenue Framework

### 1.1 Core Philosophy

Predictable Revenue, written by Aaron Ross and Marylou Tyler, is known as "The Sales Bible of Silicon Valley." The methodology helped Aaron Ross generate $100M in recurring revenue at Salesforce.com. The fundamental insight:

> **The most common misunderstood belief in outbound sales is that to sell more, you need more salespeople. In reality, lead generation is what drives growth; salespeople are simply a conduit for that growth.**

The framework creates consistency year-over-year through a formulaic process -- not last-minute hustling and guessing.

### 1.2 Cold Calling 2.0: Why Cold Calls Are Dead

Cold Calling 2.0 is an outbound sales methodology that generates new business **without using traditional cold calls**. Instead, it relies on email-first prospecting with a referral strategy.

**The key differentiator:** Instead of cold-calling a decision maker and pitching, you email a senior contact (above your target) and ask them to **refer you down** to the right person. This means:

- You know you are connecting with the right prospect
- They already know who you are when you finally connect
- They have context before your first conversation
- The internal referral carries implicit trust

#### The 5-Step Cold Calling 2.0 Process

**Step 1: Build Your Ideal Customer Profile (ICP)**
- Define 3-5 targeting criteria
- Identify core prospect challenges
- Establish deal-breaker signals
- Focus efforts on the most qualified prospects

**Step 2: Build Your Target List**
- Use prospecting tools (LinkedIn Sales Navigator, Apollo, ZoomInfo)
- Target decision-makers aligned with ICP
- Target the referral source (one level above the decision maker)

**Step 3: Run Outbound Email Campaigns**
- Send 50-100 prospecting emails per day (150-250/week maximum)
- Target 5-10 daily responses (~10% response rate)
- Segment markets by business model, revenue, title
- Keep emails short, text-based, mobile-optimized
- Include credibility examples and a single closing question
- **Goal: Receive an internal referral, NOT close a deal**

**Step 4: Sell the Dream**
- Help prospects envision solutions
- Connect product to business issues
- Ask open-ended discovery questions about current systems, challenges, decision-makers
- Always call below C-suite initially (after referral)

**Step 5: Pass the Baton (Handoff to AE)**
- SDR hands off when qualification criteria are met
- AE re-qualifies on first call ("double-qualified")
- Compensation tied to AE-accepted opportunities

### 1.3 The 3 Types of Leads: Seeds, Nets, Spears

| Type | Source | Volume | Conversion | Time to Develop | Effort |
|------|--------|--------|------------|-----------------|--------|
| **Seeds** | Word-of-mouth, referrals, organic (SEO, content), prior relationships | Low | Highest | Long (months/years) | Relationship-building |
| **Nets** | Inbound marketing: SEO, social media, blogging, webinars, paid ads, events | High | Medium (many unqualified) | Medium | One-to-many campaigns |
| **Spears** | Outbound prospecting: targeted lists, SDR-driven outreach | Low-Medium | Medium-High (very targeted) | Short-Medium | One-to-one human effort |

**Seeds** -- Your best customers come from word-of-mouth. They have the highest conversion rates but require time to cultivate. You cannot "force" seeds; you grow them through exceptional service and customer success.

**Nets** -- Inbound marketing casts a wide net. Not all leads will be qualified. Requires marketing investment and lead qualification infrastructure (MRRs/Inbound SDRs).

**Spears** -- Outbound prospecting through targeted lists. Very targeted, small in number. A human is always involved. This is where Cold Calling 2.0 lives.

**The ideal revenue engine runs all three simultaneously.** They are complementary -- seeds provide the highest-quality foundation, nets provide volume, spears provide targeted control over pipeline.

### 1.4 SDR Role Definition: SDRs vs. Closers

The core principle is **specialization** -- never have one person do prospecting AND closing.

| Function | SDR (Sales Development Rep) | AE (Account Executive) |
|----------|-----------------------------|------------------------|
| **Primary Job** | Generate new leads from cold/inactive accounts | Close qualified opportunities |
| **Activities** | Email, call, social touch prospecting | Discovery calls, demos, proposals, negotiations |
| **Goal** | Book qualified meetings for AEs | Convert opportunities to closed-won revenue |
| **Metric** | Qualified meetings booked, pipeline generated | Revenue closed, win rate, deal velocity |
| **Prospect State** | Cold/warm -- never heard of you | Warm/hot -- already qualified and interested |
| **Compensation** | Per-meeting or per-qualified-opportunity | Commission on closed revenue |

**Three specialized roles recommended by Predictable Revenue:**

1. **Outbound SDR** -- Prospects cold/inactive accounts exclusively
2. **Market Response Rep (Inbound SDR/MRR)** -- Qualifies inbound marketing leads
3. **Account Executive** -- Closes qualified opportunities ONLY

### 1.5 The Handoff: When and How SDR Passes to AE

#### When to Handoff (Qualification Criteria)

An SDR passes the lead when ALL conditions are met:

1. **Company fits the Ideal Client Profile (ICP)**
2. **Contact has influence or decision-making power**
3. **Clear interest in a next step** (e.g., willing to schedule a discovery call)
4. **No fundamental red flags or deal-breakers**
5. **Potential deal size meets minimum threshold** (e.g., 20+ users at Salesforce)
6. **Lead was clearly generated by the SDR** (not inbound or from another SDR)

#### How to Handoff (Ranked by Effectiveness)

1. **BEST: Hot Transfer** -- SDR transfers the live call directly to the AE
2. **GOOD: Scheduled Meeting** -- SDR books a specific time on both calendars
3. **LAST RESORT: Email Introduction** -- SDR sends an email connecting prospect and AE

#### The Audit Process

After handoff:
- AE re-qualifies the prospect on the first call
- This creates a "double-qualified" opportunity
- Verification confirms: outbound origin, AE qualification by phone, both SDR and AE entered notes into CRM
- This ensures solid ROI, data integrity, and quality of work

### 1.6 Metrics That Matter

#### Response & Engagement Metrics

| Metric | Benchmark | Top Performer |
|--------|-----------|---------------|
| Cold email reply rate | 2-5% | 8-15% |
| Signal-based email reply rate | 15%+ | 18%+ |
| Cold call connect rate | 5-8% | 15-25% (direct dials) |
| LinkedIn response rate | 10-15% | 25%+ |
| Meeting show rate (outbound) | 65-75% | 80-85% |

#### Pipeline & Revenue Metrics

| Metric | Benchmark | Top Performer |
|--------|-----------|---------------|
| Qualified meetings/month (outbound SDR) | 8-10 | 15-20+ |
| Qualified meetings/month (inbound SDR) | 20-25 | 35+ |
| Pipeline generated/month (SMB) | $150K-$300K | $400K+ |
| Pipeline generated/month (Mid-Market) | $300K-$600K | $800K+ |
| Pipeline generated/month (Enterprise) | $500K-$1.5M | $2M+ |
| SDR-sourced win rate | 10-20% | 25-30% |
| Pipeline coverage ratio | 3x quota | 4-5x quota |

#### Activity vs. Outcome Metrics

**Leading Indicators (Activity -- predict future results):**
- Calls made, emails sent, social touches
- Conversations had, response rates
- Meeting conversion rate, lead response time

**Lagging Indicators (Outcome -- confirm past results):**
- Revenue closed, win rate
- Customer Acquisition Cost (CAC)
- Pipeline-to-Revenue conversion

**Recommended balance:** ~60% leading indicators (for course-correction) and ~40% lagging indicators (to confirm outcomes).

---

## 2. Outbound Email Framework

### 2.1 The Referral Email Technique (Aaron Ross's Signature Move)

The most powerful technique in Predictable Revenue is NOT emailing the decision maker directly. Instead:

1. **Identify the decision maker's boss** (e.g., if you want the VP Sales, email the CRO/CEO)
2. **Send a short referral request email**
3. **The boss forwards your email down** to the right person
4. **The right person responds** -- already knowing who you are

This works because:
- Executives are helpful by nature -- a simple referral request is easy to action
- The referred person feels compelled to respond (their boss forwarded it)
- You bypass gatekeepers entirely
- You build credibility through an internal referral chain

### 2.2 Subject Lines That Work

**Proven Subject Line Formulas:**

| Format | Example | Why It Works |
|--------|---------|--------------|
| Quick question | `Quick question, {{first_name}}` | Creates curiosity gap -- they don't know what the question is |
| Referral | `{{Mutual Contact}} suggested I reach out` | Borrows trust; 46% open rate for referral-framed subjects |
| Direction request | `Can you point me in the right direction?` | Low-threat, easy to respond to |
| Specific trigger | `Re: your hiring for {{role}}` | Shows research; feels relevant |
| Value-specific | `Quick idea for {{goal}}` | Promises immediate value |
| One-word | `{{Company name}}` or `Question` | Curiosity + simplicity |
| Pain-point | `Quick solution for {{Company}}'s {{pain}}` | Direct relevance |

**Rules for subject lines:**
- Under 7 words performs best
- Create an "open loop" in the reader's mind
- Avoid spam triggers: "free", "limited time", "act now"
- Personalization in subject line increases open rate by 22%
- Test 2-3 variations per campaign

### 2.3 Cold Email Templates

#### Template 1: The Referral Request (Predictable Revenue Classic)

```
Subject: Quick question, {{first_name}}

Hi {{first_name}},

I'm reaching out because we help companies like {{similar_company_1}} 
and {{similar_company_2}} with {{specific_outcome}}.

Would you be so kind as to tell me who is responsible for 
{{function/pain_point}} at {{company}} and how I might get in touch 
with them?

Thanks,
{{your_name}}
```

**Why it works:** Aims high, asks for a referral (not a meeting), low-commitment CTA, short.

#### Template 2: The Value-First Introduction

```
Subject: {{Personalized trigger}} for {{Company}}

Hi {{first_name}},

Noticed {{specific observation about their company -- hiring, 
product launch, LinkedIn post, etc.}}.

We recently helped {{similar_company}} achieve {{specific_result 
with number}} by {{how you helped}}.

Would it make sense to share how we did it? Happy to send a 
one-pager if useful.

{{your_name}}
```

**Why it works:** Opens with research, proves value with case study, low-commitment CTA (one-pager, not a meeting).

#### Template 3: Follow-Up #1 (Value Add -- Day 3)

```
Subject: Re: {{original subject}}

Hi {{first_name}},

Wanted to share something that might be relevant -- we recently 
published a {{case study/article/guide}} on how {{similar_company}} 
solved {{pain_point}} and achieved {{result}}.

Here's the link: {{link}}

Would love to hear if you're experiencing something similar.

{{your_name}}
```

**Why it works:** Adds new value instead of "just checking in." Provides a reason to engage.

#### Template 4: Follow-Up #2 (Social Proof -- Day 7-10)

```
Subject: How {{similar_company}} approached {{relevant_topic}}

Hi {{first_name}},

Quick data point: {{similar_company}} was dealing with 
{{pain_point}} and after working with us, they saw:

- {{metric_1}}: {{result_1}}
- {{metric_2}}: {{result_2}}

If you're dealing with something similar, happy to walk you 
through what they did differently. 15 min -- no pitch.

{{your_name}}
```

**Why it works:** Concrete numbers build credibility. "No pitch" lowers resistance.

#### Template 5: Follow-Up #3 (Direct Ask -- Day 14-17)

```
Subject: Worth a quick chat?

Hi {{first_name}},

I know you're busy, so I'll be direct.

We help {{ICP description}} with {{core value prop}}. Based on 
what I've seen at {{company}}, there might be an opportunity to 
{{specific improvement}}.

Would you be open to a 15-minute call this week to explore? 
If not, I completely understand -- just let me know and I'll 
stop reaching out.

{{your_name}}
```

**Why it works:** Respects their time. Direct. Gives them an easy out (which paradoxically increases responses).

#### Template 6: The Break-Up Email (Day 21-24)

```
Subject: Should I close the file?

Hi {{first_name}},

I've reached out a few times and haven't heard back -- which 
usually means one of three things:

1. You're not the right person (happy for a redirect)
2. You're interested but the timing isn't right
3. You've been attacked by a herd of cats (hoping this isn't it)

Either way, I don't want to be a bother. Just let me know and 
I'll update my notes.

All the best,
{{your_name}}

P.S. If you'd prefer to stay connected, I share {{valuable 
content type}} on {{LinkedIn/newsletter}} -- feel free to follow.
```

**Why it works:** Humor disarms. The three options make it easy to respond. "Close the file" creates urgency. 40%+ of total sequence replies often come from this email.

#### Template 7: The "Is This the Right Person?" (Referral Redirect)

```
Subject: Right person?

Hi {{first_name}},

I've been trying to reach the person who handles 
{{function/area}} at {{company}}.

Is that you, or could you point me to the right person?

Thanks,
{{your_name}}
```

**Why it works:** Ultra-short. Easy to forward. Even if they are the right person, they often respond to clarify.

### 2.4 Email Cadence: Timing, Frequency, Channel Mix

#### The "Widening Gap" Cadence (2026 Best Practice)

Gaps between emails increase with each step to avoid looking automated:

| Touch | Channel | Day | Notes |
|-------|---------|-----|-------|
| 1 | Email (First touch) | Day 0 | Value-first introduction |
| 2 | LinkedIn (Connection request) | Day 1 | Short, relevant note |
| 3 | Email (Follow-up #1) | Day 3 | New value / case study |
| 4 | Phone (Warm call) | Day 5 | Reference the email |
| 5 | Email (Follow-up #2) | Day 10 | Social proof / data |
| 6 | LinkedIn (Engage with content) | Day 12 | Comment on their post |
| 7 | Email (Follow-up #3) | Day 17 | Direct ask |
| 8 | Phone (Final attempt) | Day 20 | Leave voicemail |
| 9 | Email (Break-up) | Day 24 | "Should I close the file?" |

#### The 3-7-7 Schedule (Minimal Cadence)

Day 0 -> Day 3 -> Day 10 -> Day 17

This captures 93% of total replies by day 10. Additional follow-ups after day 17 produce marginal or negative returns.

#### Key Timing Rules

- **Best send days:** Tuesday through Thursday
- **Best send times:** 10 AM to 2 PM (prospect's local timezone)
- **Max emails per mailbox per day:** Under 100 (to protect sender reputation)
- **Vary send times:** Never send at the exact same time (triggers spam detection)
- **Lead response time:** Under 5 minutes = 21x more likely to qualify

### 2.5 Personalization at Scale

**The Tiered Approach:**

| Tier | Accounts | Personalization Level | Time/Email |
|------|----------|-----------------------|------------|
| **Tier 1** (Top 20%) | High-value ICP-perfect | Hyper-personalized: LinkedIn research, recent posts, company news, custom video | 10-15 min |
| **Tier 2** (Middle 50%) | Good-fit ICP | Semi-personalized: Industry + role + one specific detail | 3-5 min |
| **Tier 3** (Bottom 30%) | Broad ICP match | Template + dynamic fields (name, company, industry) | 30 sec |

**What to personalize:**
- A recent LinkedIn post they published or engaged with
- A specific company achievement or challenge
- A mutual connection or shared experience
- Industry-specific pain point with their role context
- Technology they use (visible on their website or job postings)

**2026 AI-assisted approach:** AI platforms now handle ~80% of research and sequencing work. AI generates personalized email drafts based on LinkedIn profiles, company data, and intent signals. Human reps review, edit, and send.

---

## 3. SDR Playbook Structure

### 3.1 Daily Routine

#### The Ideal SDR Day (8-Hour Block)

| Time Block | Activity | Duration |
|------------|----------|----------|
| 8:00-8:30 | CRM hygiene: update notes, log activities, review pipeline | 30 min |
| 8:30-9:00 | Research & list building: identify new prospects, enrich data | 30 min |
| 9:00-10:30 | **Power Hour #1:** Outbound calls (highest connect rates 9-11 AM) | 90 min |
| 10:30-11:00 | Email personalization & sends (Tier 1 accounts) | 30 min |
| 11:00-11:30 | LinkedIn engagement: connection requests, comments, InMails | 30 min |
| 11:30-12:00 | Follow-up on warm leads, respond to inbound replies | 30 min |
| 12:00-1:00 | Lunch + learning (podcasts, training) | 60 min |
| 1:00-2:30 | **Power Hour #2:** Outbound calls + email sends | 90 min |
| 2:30-3:00 | Video prospecting: record Loom/Vidyard for Tier 1 accounts | 30 min |
| 3:00-3:30 | Multi-channel follow-ups: WhatsApp, social, voicemail | 30 min |
| 3:30-4:00 | End-of-day CRM update, plan tomorrow's targets | 30 min |

#### Daily Activity Benchmarks (2026)

| Activity | Average | Top Performer |
|----------|---------|---------------|
| Cold calls | 40-60 dials | 80-100 dials |
| Emails sent | 30-50 | 60-80 |
| LinkedIn messages | 15-25 | 30-40 |
| Total multi-channel touches | 80-120 | 150+ |
| Quality conversations | 3-5 | 8-10 |
| Meetings booked (daily average) | 0.5-0.7 | 1.0+ |

### 3.2 ICP Definition Framework (15 Criteria)

#### Firmographic Criteria

| # | Criterion | Description | Example |
|---|-----------|-------------|---------|
| 1 | **Industry/Vertical** | Which industries are best-fit | Healthcare, SaaS, Financial Services |
| 2 | **Company Size (Employees)** | Headcount range | 50-500 employees |
| 3 | **Annual Revenue** | Revenue band | R$5M-R$50M |
| 4 | **Geography** | Location/regions served | Brazil (Southeast), LATAM |
| 5 | **Growth Stage** | Company lifecycle | Series A-C, post-PMF |
| 6 | **Business Model** | How they make money | B2B SaaS, Professional Services |

#### Technographic Criteria

| # | Criterion | Description | Example |
|---|-----------|-------------|---------|
| 7 | **Tech Stack** | Tools they currently use | HubSpot, Salesforce, no CRM |
| 8 | **Digital Maturity** | How sophisticated their digital ops are | Active on social, has website, runs ads |

#### Demographic/Buyer Persona Criteria

| # | Criterion | Description | Example |
|---|-----------|-------------|---------|
| 9 | **Target Title/Role** | Who you sell to | CEO, CMO, VP Sales, Marketing Director |
| 10 | **Reporting Structure** | Who they report to | Reports to C-suite, is C-suite |
| 11 | **Decision Authority** | Can they sign a contract? | Budget owner, influencer, champion |

#### Behavioral/Situational Criteria

| # | Criterion | Description | Example |
|---|-----------|-------------|---------|
| 12 | **Pain Points** | Problems they experience | High CAC, low conversion, no follow-up |
| 13 | **Buying Triggers** | Events that create urgency | New hire, funding round, competitor move |
| 14 | **Current Solution** | What they use now (or don't) | Manual process, competitor product, nothing |
| 15 | **Disqualifiers** | Red flags that mean "don't pursue" | No budget, wrong industry, too small |

#### ICP Impact on Performance

- ICP-aligned opportunities close 2-3x more frequently than non-ICP deals
- ICP accounts move through qualification and decision faster due to better fit
- Customers matching ICP criteria churn less and expand more consistently

### 3.3 Lead Scoring Model

#### Qualification Frameworks

**BANT (Best for SDR Initial Qualification)**

| Criterion | Question | Score |
|-----------|----------|-------|
| **Budget** | Do they have budget for this? | 0-25 |
| **Authority** | Is this person a decision maker? | 0-25 |
| **Need** | Do they have an articulated need? | 0-25 |
| **Timeline** | Are they ready to buy within our sales cycle? | 0-25 |

Score 75+ = Qualified, pass to AE.
Score 50-74 = Nurture, keep in sequence.
Score <50 = Disqualify or long-term nurture.

**MEDDIC (Best for AE Deep Qualification)**

| Criterion | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| **Metrics** | What quantifiable results do they expect? |
| **Economic Buyer** | Who controls the budget? |
| **Decision Criteria** | What factors drive their decision? |
| **Decision Process** | What steps do they follow to buy? |
| **Identify Pain** | What specific pain are they experiencing? |
| **Champion** | Who inside will advocate for your solution? |

**Recommended approach:** SDRs use BANT for initial screening, AEs use MEDDIC for deeper discovery.

### 3.4 CRM Hygiene & Pipeline Management

#### Daily CRM Habits

1. **Log every activity** within 5 minutes of completion (call, email, meeting)
2. **Update contact status** immediately when disposition changes
3. **Add notes** from every conversation (key pain points, objections, next steps)
4. **Move deals** through pipeline stages in real-time
5. **Clean bounced emails** daily (protects sender reputation)

#### Weekly Pipeline Review

- Review all active deals: is the stage accurate?
- Identify stalled opportunities (no activity in 7+ days)
- Score pipeline quality: what % is ICP-aligned?
- Update close dates based on latest conversations
- Remove dead opportunities (don't let zombie deals inflate pipeline)

#### Quarterly Full Audit

- Dedup contacts and accounts
- Verify all required fields are populated
- Review and clean up tags, labels, and lifecycle stages
- Audit lead sources for accuracy
- Validate pipeline coverage ratio

#### Data Entry Standards

- Use dropdowns and picklists (not free text) for key fields
- Standardize job titles, industries, and company names
- Required fields before stage change: contact info, notes, disposition codes, next steps
- Automate status transitions where possible (reply = update stage automatically)

### 3.5 Activity Metrics vs. Outcome Metrics

#### Activity Metrics (Leading Indicators)

| Metric | What It Measures | Target |
|--------|------------------|--------|
| Calls made | Dial volume | 40-60/day |
| Emails sent | Outreach volume | 30-50/day |
| LinkedIn touches | Social engagement | 15-25/day |
| Conversations had | Actual connections | 3-5/day |
| Sequence completion rate | Follow-through | 40-60% |
| Lead response time | Speed to first touch | <5 min (inbound), <24h (outbound) |

#### Outcome Metrics (Lagging Indicators)

| Metric | What It Measures | Target |
|--------|------------------|--------|
| Meetings booked | Output of activity | 10-15/month |
| Meeting show rate | Quality of booking | 75-85% |
| Pipeline generated ($) | Revenue potential created | $150K-$600K/month |
| SDR-sourced win rate | Lead quality indicator | 15-20% |
| Pipeline-to-revenue conversion | End-to-end effectiveness | 15-25% |
| Cost per meeting | Efficiency | Track & optimize |

#### Efficiency Metrics (Conversion Ratios)

| Metric | Benchmark |
|--------|-----------|
| Dials per meeting booked | 80-120 |
| Emails per meeting booked | 150-250 |
| LinkedIn messages per meeting | 50-100 |
| Multi-channel touches per meeting | 40-80 |
| Accounts worked per meeting | 10-20 |

---

## 4. Modern SDR Techniques (2024-2026)

### 4.1 Video Prospecting (Loom, Vidyard)

**What it is:** SDRs record short, personalized videos as part of their outreach sequences, sent via email, LinkedIn, or messaging apps.

**Impact:** Organizations using video in prospecting achieve 32% higher meeting-booking rates.

#### The 45-Second Video Framework

```
[0-5 sec]  HOOK: "Hey {{first_name}}, quick 45-second video for you."
[5-15 sec] TRIGGER: "I noticed {{specific thing about their company/post}}."
[15-30 sec] VALUE: "We helped {{similar company}} achieve {{result}} by {{method}}."
[30-40 sec] CTA: "Would it make sense to grab 15 minutes this week?"
[40-45 sec] CLOSE: "Either way, hope this was useful. Talk soon."
```

#### Best Practices

- **Tiered approach:** Hyper-personalized video for Tier 1 accounts, template video for Tier 2-3
- **Email wrapper:** Subject: `{{first_name}} - quick video about {{trigger}}` / Body: 2-3 sentences + video link + soft CTA
- **Tools:** Loom (quick, easy), Vidyard (CRM integration, viewer tracking)
- **Show their website/LinkedIn** on screen while recording (proves personalization)
- **Use pause and trim** to clean up delivery

### 4.2 Social Selling Integration (LinkedIn, Instagram)

#### LinkedIn Social Selling Process

**Phase 1: Profile Optimization**
- Professional photo + banner
- Headline that speaks to prospect's pain (not your job title)
- Summary focused on how you help, not what you sell
- Featured section with case studies and testimonials

**Phase 2: Warm Engagement (Before Outreach)**
- Like and comment on prospect's posts for 1-2 weeks
- Share valuable content in your feed
- Join the same groups
- Engage with their company page content

**Phase 3: Connection + Messaging**
- Send connection request (with or without note -- test both)
- After acceptance: thank them, continue engaging with their content
- Wait 2-5 days before first DM
- DM with value, not a pitch

**LinkedIn Stats (2026):**
- LinkedIn message response rate: ~10.3% (vs 5% for cold email)
- 78% of businesses using social selling outsell their peers
- 51% more likely to hit sales quotas with social selling
- Sales Navigator AI suggests buyer groups, surfaces intent signals, and recommends lookalike accounts

#### Instagram Social Selling (Especially for Brazilian Market)

- Engage with stories and posts before DM
- Use voice notes for personal touch
- Comment genuinely on their content
- Share relevant content via DM
- Instagram is the #1 platform for B2B discovery in Brazil (57% of searches)

### 4.3 WhatsApp/Messaging Prospecting

**WhatsApp in Brazil:**
- 147 million users (2nd highest globally)
- 84% of Brazilian digital companies use WhatsApp to sell
- 61% of B2B companies in Brazil use WhatsApp
- Open rates: up to 98%
- Replies often within minutes

**Important legal note:** Under LGPD (Brazil's data protection law), you need explicit consent to message someone via WhatsApp Business. First touch should come from the prospect.

**Workaround strategies:**
- Collect WhatsApp number during lead generation (forms, events)
- Move warm LinkedIn/email prospects to WhatsApp
- Use WhatsApp as a follow-up channel after initial engagement
- Never cold-message on WhatsApp without prior interaction

### 4.4 AI-Assisted Prospecting (2026)

**How AI is changing SDR work:**

| Task | Before AI | With AI (2026) |
|------|-----------|----------------|
| Research | 10-15 min/prospect | 30 sec (automated enrichment) |
| Email personalization | 5-10 min/email | 1-2 min (AI draft + human review) |
| Lead scoring | Manual BANT | Real-time intent signals + predictive scoring |
| Sequencing | Manual cadence setup | AI-optimized send times + channel selection |
| Follow-up timing | Calendar reminders | AI identifies optimal re-engagement windows |

**Key AI tools (2026):**
- Apollo, Clay, Instantly (email + sequencing)
- Gong, Chorus (conversation intelligence)
- Sales Navigator AI (buyer signals)
- ChatGPT/Claude (email drafting, research)
- 6sense, Bombora (intent data)

**AI now handles ~80% of research and sequencing work.** Human reps focus on high-value conversations, relationship building, and creative problem-solving.

### 4.5 Multi-Threading (Reaching Multiple Stakeholders)

**What it is:** Engaging multiple stakeholders within a target account simultaneously, rather than relying on a single point of contact.

**Win rate impact:**
- Single-threaded deals: **5% close rate**
- Multi-threaded deals (5+ stakeholders): **30% close rate**
- That is a **6x difference**
- Cross-department threading: 56% win rate increase
- Enterprise deals involve 11-13 stakeholders on average
- Won strategic deals average 17 contacts engaged

#### 3-Phase Implementation

**Phase 1: Build Your Champion (Touchpoints 1-2)**
- Identify someone experiencing the pain, understanding impact, able to navigate internal politics
- A true champion maps the buying committee and anticipates competing priorities

**Phase 2: Expand to Buying Committee (Touchpoint 3+)**
- Don't lead with executives (drops win rate by 6%)
- Introduce executives around the third touchpoint (increases win rate by 5%)
- Target 3-5 stakeholders minimum: champion, economic buyer, 1-2 technical/functional evaluators

**Phase 3: Role-Specific Messaging**

| Stakeholder | They Care About | Your Message Focus |
|-------------|-----------------|-------------------|
| End User | Daily workflow improvement | "Here's how this saves you 2 hours/day" |
| Budget Holder | ROI and cost justification | "Here's the financial impact analysis" |
| IT Evaluator | Security, integration, implementation | "Here's our architecture and compliance" |
| Executive Sponsor | Strategic alignment | "Here's how this drives your company's goals" |

**Tactical move:** Draft introduction emails for your champion to forward to other stakeholders. Include problem summary, conversation rationale, and specific 30-minute meeting agenda.

---

## 5. Pipeline Math

### 5.1 Revenue Goal -> Pipeline -> Meetings -> Contacts

The fundamental formula for predictable revenue:

```
ANNUAL REVENUE TARGET
        |
        v
PIPELINE NEEDED (3-5x revenue target)
        |
        v
OPPORTUNITIES NEEDED (Pipeline / Avg Deal Size)
        |
        v
MEETINGS NEEDED (Opportunities / Meeting-to-Opp Rate)
        |
        v
CONTACTS NEEDED (Meetings / Contact-to-Meeting Rate)
        |
        v
ACTIVITIES NEEDED (Contacts / Activity-to-Contact Rate)
```

### 5.2 Worked Example

**Goal:** R$1.2M annual revenue

```
Annual Revenue Target:              R$1,200,000
Average Deal Size:                  R$10,000/month = R$120,000/year
Close Rate:                         20%
Meeting-to-Opportunity Rate:        25%
Contact-to-Meeting Rate:            5%
                                    ─────────────────

Deals Needed:                       R$1,200,000 / R$120,000 = 10 deals
Pipeline Needed (3x):               10 / 20% = 50 opportunities × R$120K = R$6,000,000
Meetings Needed:                    50 / 25% = 200 qualified meetings
Contacts Needed:                    200 / 5% = 4,000 contacts reached
Monthly Meetings:                   200 / 12 = ~17 meetings/month
Monthly Contacts:                   4,000 / 12 = ~334 contacts/month
SDRs Needed:                        17 meetings / 12 meetings per SDR = ~1.5 SDRs
```

### 5.3 Conversion Benchmarks by Channel

| Channel | Contact-to-Reply Rate | Reply-to-Meeting Rate | Contact-to-Meeting Rate |
|---------|----------------------|----------------------|------------------------|
| Cold Email | 2-5% | 20-30% | 0.4-1.5% |
| Cold Call | 5-12% connect | 10-20% | 0.5-2.4% |
| LinkedIn InMail | 10-15% | 15-25% | 1.5-3.75% |
| Referral/Warm Intro | 30-50% | 40-60% | 12-30% |
| Multi-Channel Sequence | 4-7% meeting rate | -- | 4-7% |
| Video Prospecting | 15-25% view rate | 10-15% | 1.5-3.75% |

**Key insight:** Multi-channel sequences convert at 2-3x higher than any single channel alone.

### 5.4 How to Forecast Based on Pipeline

**Pipeline Coverage Ratio:**
```
Pipeline Coverage = Total Pipeline Value / Sales Quota

Target: 3-5x coverage

Example:
Quarterly quota:          R$300,000
Required pipeline:        R$900,000 - R$1,500,000
```

**Revenue Forecast Formula:**
```
Forecasted Revenue = Pipeline Value × Win Rate × (1 - Slip Rate)

Example:
Pipeline:                 R$1,200,000
Win Rate:                 20%
Slip Rate:                15%
Forecast:                 R$1,200,000 × 20% × 85% = R$204,000
```

**Pipeline Velocity:**
```
Pipeline Velocity = (# Opportunities × Avg Deal Size × Win Rate) / Sales Cycle Length (days)

Example:
50 opps × R$120,000 × 20% / 90 days = R$13,333/day velocity
```

**Healthy Pipeline Indicators:**
- 3-5x quota coverage at start of quarter
- No single deal represents >20% of pipeline
- Stage distribution follows a funnel shape (more early-stage than late-stage)
- Average deal age does not exceed 1.5x average sales cycle
- Pipeline creation rate exceeds close rate

---

## 6. Specialization Model

### 6.1 The Four Specialized Roles

| Role | Primary Function | Skills Required | Metrics |
|------|-----------------|-----------------|---------|
| **Inbound SDR (MRR)** | Qualify marketing-generated leads | Speed, qualification, CRM skills | Response time, MQL-to-SQL rate, meetings booked |
| **Outbound SDR (BDR)** | Prospect cold/inactive accounts | Persistence, research, creativity | Activities, meetings booked, pipeline generated |
| **Account Executive (AE)** | Close qualified opportunities | Discovery, negotiation, deal management | Revenue closed, win rate, deal velocity |
| **Customer Success Manager (CSM)** | Retain and expand customers | Relationship, product knowledge, analytics | Retention rate, NRR, upsell revenue |

### 6.2 When to Specialize

**Aaron Ross's principle:** "If you have more than one sales development rep, you need to split inbound from outbound."

| Company Stage | Revenue | Team Size | Recommendation |
|---------------|---------|-----------|----------------|
| **Founder-Led** | <R$1M | 1-2 people | Founder does everything. No specialization yet. |
| **First SDR** | R$1-3M | 2-5 people | Hire 1 SDR (hybrid inbound/outbound). AE = founder. |
| **Split Roles** | R$3-5M | 5-10 people | Separate inbound SDR from outbound SDR. Hire first dedicated AE. |
| **Full Specialization** | R$5M+ | 10+ people | Full 4-role model. SDR team, AE team, CSM team. |
| **Scaling** | R$10M+ | 20+ people | SDR managers, team leads, regional pods. |

**Key benchmarks:**
- Among B2B SaaS companies >R$5M revenue: 67% have an SDR team
- Among companies with ACV >R$100K: 89% have SDR teams
- Recommended SDR-to-AE ratio: 2:1

### 6.3 Compensation Structures (2026 Benchmarks)

#### SDR Compensation

| Level | Base Salary (USD) | OTE (USD) | Variable % | Variable Structure |
|-------|-------------------|-----------|------------|-------------------|
| SDR (0-1 yr) | $45K-$55K | $65K-$80K | 30-40% | Per qualified meeting + pipeline bonus |
| Senior SDR (1-3 yr) | $55K-$70K | $80K-$100K | 30-40% | Per qualified meeting + pipeline + win bonus |
| SDR Manager | $85K-$110K | $120K-$150K | 25-35% | Team performance + pipeline + revenue |

**Recommended variable split for SDRs:**
- 70% -- Qualified meetings booked
- 20% -- Pipeline generated ($)
- 10% -- Activity/CRM hygiene score

#### AE Compensation

| Level | Base Salary (USD) | OTE (USD) | Variable % | Commission Rate |
|-------|-------------------|-----------|------------|-----------------|
| AE (SMB) | $60K-$80K | $120K-$160K | 45-50% | 8-10% of ACV |
| AE (Mid-Market) | $80K-$100K | $160K-$200K | 50% | 10-12% of ACV |
| AE (Enterprise) | $100K-$130K | $200K-$280K | 50-55% | 11.5% average of ACV |

**Notes for Brazilian context:** Adjust salary ranges based on local market. SDR salaries in Brazil typically range from R$3,000-R$8,000/month base + variable. The ratio structure (base vs. variable split) should remain similar.

#### CSM Compensation

| Level | Base Salary (USD) | OTE (USD) | Variable % |
|-------|-------------------|-----------|------------|
| CSM | $60K-$80K | $80K-$100K | 20-25% |
| Senior CSM | $80K-$100K | $105K-$130K | 20-25% |

Variable typically tied to: retention rate, NRR (Net Revenue Retention), and expansion/upsell revenue.

## 7. Key Scripts & Templates

### 7.1 Cold Email Templates (Complete Set)

#### Email 1: The Referral Request

```
Subject: Quick question, {{first_name}}

Hi {{first_name}},

I'm writing to find out who handles {{area/function}} at 
{{company}}.

We work with companies like {{reference_1}} and {{reference_2}} 
to {{key_outcome}}, and I'd love to explore if we could help 
{{company}} as well.

Could you point me in the right direction?

Thanks,
{{your_name}}
{{your_title}} | {{your_company}}
```

#### Email 2: The Trigger-Based Opener

```
Subject: Re: {{company}}'s {{trigger_event}}

Hi {{first_name}},

Congrats on {{trigger: new hire, funding, expansion, product launch}}.

When companies like yours hit this stage, they usually face 
{{common_challenge}}. We helped {{similar_company}} navigate this 
and achieve {{specific_result}}.

Would it be useful to share what we learned?

{{your_name}}
```

#### Email 3: The PAS (Problem-Agitate-Solve)

```
Subject: {{Pain point}} at {{company}}?

Hi {{first_name}},

Most {{title}}s I talk to are dealing with {{problem}}.

What makes it worse is {{agitation: consequences, wasted money, 
lost opportunities, team frustration}}.

We built {{your_solution}} specifically to solve this. 
{{Similar_company}} went from {{before_state}} to {{after_state}} 
in {{timeframe}}.

Worth a 15-minute conversation?

{{your_name}}
```

#### Email 4: The Social Proof Bomb

```
Subject: How {{similar_company}} solved {{problem}}

Hi {{first_name}},

{{Similar_company}} was struggling with {{same_problem_prospect_has}}.

In {{timeframe}}, they:
- {{Result_1 with number}}
- {{Result_2 with number}}
- {{Result_3 with number}}

Happy to share exactly what they did. Would a quick call 
make sense?

{{your_name}}
```

#### Email 5: The "One-Liner" Follow-Up

```
Subject: Re: {{original_subject}}

Hi {{first_name}}, did my last note land at a bad time? 
Happy to reconnect when it makes sense. -- {{your_name}}
```

#### Email 6: The Break-Up

```
Subject: Closing the loop

Hi {{first_name}},

I've reached out a few times without hearing back. I'll 
assume the timing isn't right and will close my file.

If things change in the future, feel free to reach out. 
I'm always happy to help.

All the best,
{{your_name}}

P.S. If someone else at {{company}} would be a better fit 
for this conversation, I'd appreciate the introduction.
```

### 7.2 LinkedIn Scripts

#### Connection Request (With Note -- 300 char limit)

```
Hi {{first_name}}, I came across your work at {{company}} -- 
particularly {{specific_thing}}. I work with {{ICP_description}} 
on {{outcome}} and would love to connect. -- {{your_name}}
```

#### Connection Request (Without Note)

Research shows 34.3% acceptance rate without a note vs. 32.3% with a note. Test both. When in doubt, no note + engage with their content first.

#### LinkedIn DM #1 (After Connection Accepted -- Wait 2-3 Days)

```
Thanks for connecting, {{first_name}}!

I noticed {{specific observation about their company/post}}.

We recently helped {{similar_company}} with {{challenge}} and they 
achieved {{result}}. Thought it might be relevant.

Would you be open to a quick chat? No pressure either way.
```

#### LinkedIn DM #2 (Follow-Up -- 5-7 Days Later)

```
Hi {{first_name}}, wanted to share a quick resource.

We put together a {{guide/case study/report}} on 
{{relevant_topic}} that companies like {{their_company}} have 
found useful.

Here's the link: {{link}}

Happy to discuss if any of it resonates.
```

#### LinkedIn DM #3 (Direct Ask -- 10-14 Days Later)

```
{{first_name}}, I'll keep this brief.

Based on what I've seen at {{company}}, I think we could help 
you {{specific_outcome}}.

Would you be open to a 15-minute call this week? I promise it'll 
be worth your time.

If not now, I totally understand -- just let me know.
```

#### LinkedIn Voice Note Script (45 seconds)

```
"Hey {{first_name}}, it's {{your_name}} from {{company}}. 
Wanted to send a quick voice note instead of another text 
message. I saw {{trigger/observation}} and thought you might 
be interested in how {{similar_company}} handled a similar 
situation. If you're open to a quick chat, let me know. 
Either way, hope you have a great week."
```

### 7.3 WhatsApp First Touch Messages

**IMPORTANT:** In Brazil, WhatsApp first touch should ONLY happen after prior engagement (form fill, event, LinkedIn conversation, etc.) due to LGPD compliance.

#### After Form Fill / Lead Magnet

```
Oi {{first_name}}, tudo bem? Aqui é {{your_name}} da {{company}}.

Vi que você baixou nosso {{material/ebook/guia}} sobre {{topic}}.

Queria entender: {{question about their pain point}}?

Se quiser, posso compartilhar como {{similar_company}} resolveu 
isso. Me avisa!
```

**Translation/English version:**

```
Hi {{first_name}}, this is {{your_name}} from {{company}}.

I saw you downloaded our {{material}} about {{topic}}.

Quick question: {{question about their pain point}}?

If you're interested, I can share how {{similar_company}} 
solved this. Let me know!
```

#### After LinkedIn Connection (Moved to WhatsApp)

```
{{first_name}}, {{your_name}} aqui! Trocamos mensagem no 
LinkedIn sobre {{topic}}.

Como combinamos, estou enviando {{material/info/link}} aqui 
pelo WhatsApp pra facilitar.

Quer marcar um bate-papo rápido de 15 min essa semana?
```

#### After Event / Webinar

```
Oi {{first_name}}! Aqui é {{your_name}} da {{company}}.

Foi ótimo ter você no {{event_name}}. Queria te mandar 
{{material complementar}} que mencionamos.

Se quiser aprofundar como isso se aplica na {{their_company}}, 
posso te mostrar em 15 minutos. Tem interesse?
```

#### Follow-Up (If No Response After 3 Days)

```
{{first_name}}, sei que você deve estar corrido. Sem pressão!

Só queria deixar aqui o link do {{case_study/material}} que 
mencionei: {{link}}

Quando fizer sentido, é só me chamar. Estou por aqui! 👋
```

### 7.4 Phone Bridge Scripts (Warm Call After Email)

#### Opening (Reference the Email)

```
"Hi {{first_name}}, this is {{your_name}} from {{company}}.

I sent you an email a few days ago about {{topic}} -- 
not sure if you had a chance to see it.

The reason I'm calling is that we work with companies 
like {{similar_company}} on {{outcome}}, and I wanted to 
see if this might be relevant for {{their_company}}.

Do you have 30 seconds for me to explain why I reached out?"
```

#### After They Say "I Didn't See the Email"

```
"No worries at all! Let me give you the quick version.

We help {{ICP_description}} with {{pain_point}}. 
{{Similar_company}} was dealing with {{specific_challenge}} 
and after working with us, they {{result_with_number}}.

I'm not sure if {{their_company}} is experiencing something 
similar, but if you are, it might be worth a conversation.

Would you be open to a 15-minute call this week to explore?"
```

#### After They Say "I'm Busy"

```
"Totally understand -- I'll be quick.

In 10 seconds: we help {{ICP}} achieve {{result}}. 
I'd love 15 minutes to show you how.

Can I send a calendar invite for a time that works better?"
```

#### Objection: "Send Me an Email"

```
"Happy to! Before I do, can I ask one quick question 
so I can make the email relevant?

What's your biggest challenge right now when it comes 
to {{area}}?"

[If they answer, you now have context for a personalized email]
[If they don't, send the email and follow up in 3 days]
```

### 7.5 Meeting Booking Scripts

#### The 4-Step Launch (Gabrielle Blackwell / Predictable Revenue)

```
STEP 1 - INTRODUCTION:
"Hey {{first_name}}, my name is {{your_name}} calling from 
{{company}} on a recorded line. Did I catch you with a quick 
moment to chat?"

STEP 2 - RELEVANCE:
"The reason for my reaching out is I was doing some research 
on {{their_company}} and I saw that you're involved in 
{{their_function}}."

STEP 3 - VALUE:
"We have a solution at {{company}} that is making 
{{their_function}} a lot {{faster/easier/more efficient}} 
for companies like {{reference}}."

STEP 4 - LAUNCH:
"I'm curious -- how are you handling that today?"

[Listen. Mirror. Ask follow-up questions.]

STEP 5 - CLOSE:
"Based on what you're doing today, specifically {{process_1}} 
and {{process_2}}, and comparing that to our customers who are 
able to {{do_function_better}}, it seems like there might be 
an opportunity to optimize some things -- and that's what I 
really wanted to connect about.

Would it be worth having a conversation?"
```

#### The Poke the Bear (Josh Braun)

```
"Hi {{first_name}}, {{your_name}} here from {{company}}. 
I was hoping to speak with you briefly about {{topic}}. 
Do you have a minute?

[If yes]

Thanks. I speak with {{their_title}}s all the time who 
are {{experiencing_pain_point}}.

Quick question: how do you make sure you don't 
{{experience_pain}} when {{dealing_with_challenge}}?

[Listen. Let them talk.]

Sounds like this might make sense to you since you're 
dealing with {{pain_point}}. I know I promised to be brief.

Would it make sense to grab a few minutes on the calendar 
for a demo, so you can review your options should the need 
arise?"
```

#### The Pattern Interrupt (James Buckley)

```
"Thanks for taking the call, do you have a moment?

[This opening thanks them FIRST, which is unexpected 
and disarms the typical cold call resistance]

Great. I'll be brief. I noticed {{trigger}} and wanted 
to quickly share how we helped {{similar_company}} with 
a similar situation.

They were dealing with {{pain}} and achieved {{result}}.

Would it make sense to explore if something similar 
could work for {{their_company}}?"
```

### 7.6 Voicemail Script (30 Seconds Max)

```
"Hi {{first_name}}, this is {{your_name}} from {{company}}.

I'm calling because we help {{ICP_description}} with 
{{outcome}}, and I think there's a fit with {{their_company}}.

I'll send you an email with some details. If it resonates, 
feel free to reply or call me back at {{phone}}.

Thanks, {{first_name}}. Have a great day."
```

### 7.7 Discovery Call Opening Script

```
"Thanks for taking the time, {{first_name}}. I appreciate it.

Before we dive in, I want to make sure this is a productive 
use of your time. Here's what I'd suggest for our 30 minutes:

1. I'll ask a few questions to understand your current 
   situation and challenges
2. If it makes sense, I'll share how we've helped 
   similar companies
3. At the end, we'll decide together if there's a 
   next step -- or not. No pressure.

Sound fair?

Great. Let me start with this: what prompted you to take 
this call today?"
```

---

## 8. Brazilian B2B Context Notes

### 8.1 Channel Priorities for Brazil

| Channel | Priority | Notes |
|---------|----------|-------|
| **WhatsApp** | #1 | 147M users, 98% open rates, 84% of companies use it to sell |
| **Instagram** | #2 | 57% of B2B discovery, stories + DMs + reels |
| **LinkedIn** | #3 | Growing fast in Brazil, essential for B2B/corporate |
| **Email** | #4 | Important but secondary to WhatsApp for follow-up |
| **Phone** | #5 | Used primarily as bridge after digital engagement |

### 8.2 LGPD Compliance

Brazil's Lei Geral de Protecao de Dados (LGPD) is equivalent to GDPR. Key rules:
- **Consent required** before sending marketing messages via WhatsApp
- **Legitimate interest** can justify B2B prospecting via email/LinkedIn
- **Opt-out** must be easy and immediate
- **Data minimization** -- only collect what you need
- Never buy phone number lists for cold WhatsApp messaging

### 8.3 Cultural Adaptations

- **Relationship-first:** Brazilian B2B is more relationship-driven than US/EU. Build rapport before pitching.
- **WhatsApp culture:** Moving to WhatsApp is a sign of trust and closeness. Prospects expect it.
- **Audio messages:** Voice notes on WhatsApp are extremely common and effective in Brazil.
- **Timing:** Business hours are typically 8-18h. Avoid weekends for B2B outreach.
- **Formality spectrum:** Start formal ("senhor/senhora"), relax as relationship develops. In tech/startup, informal from the start.
- **Follow-up patience:** Brazilians may take longer to respond but are less likely to unsubscribe. Persistence is more accepted.
- **Instagram presence:** Many B2B decision-makers in Brazil are active on Instagram. "Check their Instagram" is a valid research step.

### 8.4 Recommended Cadence for Brazilian B2B

| Touch | Channel | Day | Brazilian Context |
|-------|---------|-----|-------------------|
| 1 | LinkedIn connection request | Day 0 | No note, or short note in Portuguese |
| 2 | Email (value-first) | Day 1 | In Portuguese, reference local companies |
| 3 | LinkedIn DM (after acceptance) | Day 3 | Thank them, share content |
| 4 | WhatsApp (if number available) | Day 5 | Voice note or text, reference the email |
| 5 | Email follow-up (case study) | Day 8 | Local case study preferred |
| 6 | Instagram (engage with story/post) | Day 10 | Comment, react, share |
| 7 | WhatsApp follow-up | Day 14 | Send relevant resource |
| 8 | Phone call (warm) | Day 17 | Reference all previous touchpoints |
| 9 | Email break-up | Day 21 | Casual, door-open tone |

---

## Summary: Key Takeaways

1. **Predictable Revenue is built on specialization.** Separate prospecting from closing. SDRs prospect, AEs close.

2. **Cold Calling 2.0 is email-first + referral strategy.** Aim high, ask for referrals down, never cold-pitch on first touch.

3. **Three lead types (Seeds, Nets, Spears) must work together** for a healthy pipeline. Don't rely on just one.

4. **Pipeline math is non-negotiable.** Work backwards from your revenue goal to know exactly how many activities, contacts, meetings, and opportunities you need.

5. **Multi-channel outreach converts 2-3x better** than single-channel. Combine email + phone + LinkedIn + WhatsApp + video.

6. **Multi-threading (5+ stakeholders) increases win rates by 6x.** Never rely on a single champion.

7. **In Brazil, WhatsApp is king.** Prioritize it as a follow-up channel, use Instagram for discovery, and respect LGPD.

8. **AI is transforming SDR work (2026).** 80% of research and sequencing is automated. Human value is in relationships, creativity, and judgment.

9. **Quality beats quantity.** Signal-personalized emails get 18% reply rates vs. 3.43% average. Fewer, better touches win.

10. **Metrics matter:** Track leading indicators (activities, response rates) to predict lagging indicators (revenue, win rates). Aim for 60% leading / 40% lagging in your dashboard.
